Wasiyyah — Bequest
beginner
6 min
Definition and Conditions of a Valid Will in Hanafi Fiqh
Introduces the Book of Wills and lists seven conditions for a valid will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of a will (waṣiyyah) and list all seven conditions for its validity, applying them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
A will is a deferred transfer of ownership after death, requiring seven precise conditions for validity.

This lesson introduces the Book of Wills (Kitab al-Waṣāyā) from a classical Hanafi text. We will dissect the definition of a will—a transfer of ownership postponed until after death—and examine the seven conditions that must be present for a will to be legally sound. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly drafting or evaluating a will according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key parties and object
The text introduces three terms: al-mūṣī (testator), al-mūṣā lahu (beneficiary), and al-mūṣā bihi (subject of the bequest). Identify each in the passage.
These terms recur throughout the Book of Wills.
2
Extract the definition of a will
The passage gives a Shariah definition: 'tamlīk muḍāf ilā ba‘d al-mawt bi-ṭarīq al-tabarru‘.' Break this down: tamlīk (transfer of ownership), muḍāf ilā ba‘d al-mawt (deferred to after death), bi-ṭarīq al-tabarru‘ (by way of gratuitous donation).
This definition distinguishes a will from a gift (hibah), which takes immediate effect.
3
List the seven conditions
From the bulleted list, write down each condition in order. For each, note the rationale or exception given (e.g., the fetus condition requires birth within six months; the one-third limit).
The conditions are: capacity, no debt, beneficiary alive, not an heir, not a killer, object ownable, within one-third.
4
Understand the legal effect
The text states the beneficiary becomes owner with a 'new ownership' (milk jadīd), akin to hibah, and the testator acts as the beneficiary's deputy.
This clarifies that the transfer is not merely a contract but a direct assignment.
5
Review the placement rationale
The note explains why the Book of Wills is placed at the end: death is the final stage, and it relates to crimes (jināyāt) and blood-money (diyāt).
This shows the systematic arrangement of fiqh works.

Source Text

كتاب الوصايا
ترجمہ یہ کتاب وصیت کے بیان میں ہے

The Book of Wills. Translation: This book is about the statement of wills. The Book of Wills. Chapter on the description of the will: what is permissible and what is recommended and what constitutes revocation. Translation: This book is about wills. This is a chapter on the description of the will and the contract of will that is permissible and recommended, and the statement by which revocation occurs. Explanation: al-Musī: the testator; al-Mūṣā lahu: the person for whom the will is made; al-Mūṣā bihi: the thing that is willed. Then there are several conditions for the will: 1. The testator must have the capacity to make a gratuitous donation. 2. The testator must not be in debt. 3. At the time of the will, the beneficiary must be alive, even if not yet born from the mother's womb, i.e., the will is valid for a fetus on condition that it is certainly in the womb at the time of the will, i.e., it is born within six months. 4. The beneficiary must not be an heir of the testator. 5. The beneficiary must not be the killer of the testator. 6. The bequest must be capable of being owned. 7. The bequest must not exceed one-third of the estate. And the ruling of the will is that the beneficiary becomes the owner with a new ownership, just as in the case of hibah (gift) the donee becomes owner, and the testator takes the place of the beneficiary. Note: The final stage of man is death, and the will is a matter at the time of death, for this reason it is mentioned at the end of the book. It is also related to the Book of Crimes and the Book of Blood-Money? Because crimes are sometimes a cause of death, so it was mentioned after the Book of Crimes and the Book of Blood-Money. Note: 'Wasiyyah' is a noun in the meaning of the verbal noun. Then they call the bequeathed thing 'wasiyyah'. And al-wasiyyah in Shariah is a transfer of ownership (tamlīk) deferred to after death by way of gratuitous transfer.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the Book of Wills (Kitab al-Wasaya). It opens with the chapter on the attributes of the will (Bāb fī ṣifat al-waṣiyyah). The author first defines the key terms: al-mūṣī (the testator), al-mūṣā lahu (the beneficiary), and al-mūṣā bihi (the subject of the bequest). Then seven conditions for a valid will are listed: (1) the testator must be legally capable of gratuitous transfer (tabarruʿ); (2) the testator must not be indebted (i.e., his debts do not consume the entire estate); (3) the beneficiary must be alive at the time of the will, even if an unborn child (jānīn), provided it is born within six months; (4) the beneficiary must not be an heir of the testator; (5) the beneficiary must not have killed the testator; (6) the bequest must be capable of ownership; (7) the bequest cannot exceed one-third of the estate unless the heirs consent. The definition concludes: “Al-waṣiyyah in Shariah is the assignment of ownership (tamlīk) deferred to after death, by way of gratuitous transfer (ṭarīq al-tabarruʿ).” The author also notes that the book on wills is placed near the end of the fiqh work because it relates to death, which is the final stage of life.

Key Terms
موصی (mūṣī): The person making the will (testator).
موصی لہ (mūṣā lahu): The person for whom the will is made (beneficiary).
موصی بہ (mūṣā bihi): The thing that is bequeathed (subject of the will).
وصیت (waṣiyyah): A transfer of ownership deferred to after death, by way of gratuitous transfer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which condition below is NOT required for a valid will according to this passage?
A) The testator must have the capacity to make a gratuitous donation.
B) The bequest must not exceed one-third of the estate.
C) The beneficiary must be an heir of the testator.
D) The bequest must be capable of being owned.

Key Takeaway
A valid Hanafi will requires seven conditions: capacity, no debt, beneficiary alive, beneficiary not an heir or killer, bequest ownable, and within one-third of the estate.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
The Legal Status of Wasiyyah: Mustahabb and Justified by Istihsan
States ruling that will is mustahabb, then justifies by istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wasiyyah, explain why qiyas would reject it, and describe how istihsan justifies its permissibility.

Core Idea
A will is recommended (mustahabb), not obligatory; qiyas rejects it, but istihsan overrides due to human need.

In this lesson we examine the legal status of a will (wasiyyah) according to al-Quduri. The matn declares that a will is not obligatory (wajib) but recommended (mustahabb). However, pure analogy (qiyas) would actually reject its validity. We explore this conflict between qiyas and istihsan (juristic preference) and see how the Hanafi school uses istihsan to permit the will, drawing a parallel with the contract of ijarah (lease).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on wasiyyah
Find the explicit statement from al-Quduri: does he say the will is wajib, mandub, or something else?
The text says 'al-wasiyyah ghayru wajibah wa hiya mustahabbah'.
2
Understand the qiyas analogy that rejects the will
Qiyas compares the will to a deferred transfer of ownership while ownership still exists. If saying 'I make you owner tomorrow' is invalid, then a will deferred after death is even more invalid because ownership has ceased.
The illa is tamlik mudaf (deferred transfer) to a time when ownership does not exist.
3
Recognize the need that triggers istihsan
People are often negligent due to hope (amal) and may fall into shortcomings. When illness strikes, they need to make amends through bequests. Istihsan overrides qiyas because of this need.
The text says 'fa inna al-insana maghrurun bi-amalihi'.
4
See the parallel with ijarah
Just as ijarah (lease) is permitted by istihsan despite qiyas (because it involves prepayment for future benefit), the will is also permitted by istihsan.
The text states 'wa mithluhu fi al-ijarah bayyanahu'.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The will is permissible and recommended, not obligatory. Its validity is established by istihsan, not by qiyas.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قال الوصية غير واجبة وهي مستحبة والقياس يابى جوازها لانه تملیک مضاف الى حال زوال مالكيته ولو اضيف الى حال قيامها بان قیل ملكتك غدا كان باطلا فهذا اولى الا انا استحسناه لحاجة الناس اليها فان الانسان مغرور بامله مقصر فى عمله فاذا عرض له المرض وخاف البيات يحتاج الى تلافي بعض ما فرط منه من التفريط بماله على وجه لو مضى فيه يتحقق مقصده المالى ولو انهضه البرء يصرفه الى مطلبه الحالي وفي شرع الوصية ذلك فشرعناه ومثله في الاجارة بيناه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ وصیت واجب نہیں مستحب ہے اور قیاس اس کے جواز کا انکار کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ وصیت ایسی تملیک ہے جو اس کی مالکیت کے زوال کے وقت کی جانب مضاف ہے اور اگر اس تملیک کی اضافت مالکیت کے قیام کے وقت کی جانب کی جائے اس طریقہ پر کہ کہا جائے میں نے تجھ کو کل مالک بنا دیا، تو یہ باطل ہے پس یہ بدرجہ اولی مگر ہم نے وصیت کو بناء پر استحسان جائز قرار دیا ومیت کی جانب لوگوں کی حاجت کی وجہ سے اس لئے کہ انسان اپنی امید کی وجہ سے دھو کہ میں پڑ جاتا ہے اپنے عمل میں کوتاہی کر دیتا ہے پس جب اس کو مرض عارض ہو گیا اور وہ ہلاکت سے ڈرا تو وہ اس کو تا ہی کے تدارک کا محتاج ہوتا ہے جو اس کی جانب سے مقدم ہو چکی ہیں اپنے مال کے ذریعہ اس طریقہ پر کہ اگر وہ اس مرض میں مر گیا تو اس کا اخروی مقصد تحقیق ہو جائے گا اور اگر صحت نے اس کو اٹھا دیا تو وہ اس مال کو دنیوی مقصد میں صرف کرے گا اور وصیت کے مشروع کرنے میں یہ مقصد حاصل ہے تو اس کو ہم نے مشروع قرار دیا اور اسی کے مثل اجارہ میں ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
تشریح وصیت واجب نہیں البتہ بقول مصنف مستحب ہے اور قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ وصیت جائز ہی نہ ہو۔ اس لئے کہ موصی موصی لہ کو ایسے وقت مالک بناتا ہے جب کہ موصی خود بھی مالک نہیں ہے، اور اگر کسی شخص کی ملکیت برقرار ہے مگر وہ ملکیت کی اضافت آئندہ زمانہ کی طرف کر دے اور یوں کہے کہ میں نے تجھے اس چیز کا کل آئندہ مالک بنا دیا تو یہ تملیک باطل ہے، حالانکہ ملک کی ملکیت آج بھی ہے اور کل بھی ، اس کے باوجود اسکو باطل قرار دیا گیا ہے۔
تو جہاں مرنے کے بعد ملکیت ہی نہیں رہتی وہ بدرجہ اولی باطل ہونی چاہئے ۔ بہر حال قیاس کا تقاضہ تھا، لیکن قیاس کو چھوڑ کر استحسان پر عمل کیا گیا ہے اور اس کو جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے کیونکہ لوگوں کو اس کی حاجت ہے، جیسے لوگوں کو اجارہ کی حاجت ہے اگر چہ قیاس اس کے عدم جواز کا تقاضہ کرتا ہے مگر بناء پر استحسان جیسے اجارہ کو جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے ای طرح وصیت کو جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے۔
وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ انسان کو امیدوں نے گھیر رکھا ہے جس کی وجہ سے وہ بہت سی کوتاہیاں کر دیتا ہے لیکن جب مرض میں پھنسا تو اب اس کو ندامت ہوئی تو شریعت نے اس کو اجازت دی کہ امیدوں کے چکر میں مال کے متعلق جو کوتاہیاں صادر ہوئی ہیں ان کی تلافی کر دے ، اگر وہ اس مرض میں مرجائے تو اخروی مقصد پورا ہو جائے اور اگر نہ مرے تو دینوی مقاصد میں ابھی اس کو استعمال کر
کے فائدہ اٹھائے ۔
اور وصیت کے اندر بھی یہی ہوتا ہے اس وجہ سے وصیت کو جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے۔
The legal status of the will. He (al-Qudūrī) said: The will is not obligatory but is recommended. Qiyās (analogy) rejects its permissibility because it is a transfer of ownership (tamlīk) deferred to a state of his ownership ceasing. If it were deferred to a state of its existence (i.e., ownership still present) by saying 'I make you owner tomorrow,' that would be invalid; so this (the will) is even more (invalid). However, we have declared it good (istaḥsannāhu) due to the need of people for it. For man is deceived by his hopes and deficient in his deeds. When illness befalls him and he fears perdition, he needs to make up for some of the shortcomings that preceded from him by means of his wealth, in such a way that if he dies in it, his financial objective is realized; and if recovery raises him up, he spends it on his current need. In the legislation of the will, that (objective) is found, so we legislated it. And the like of it in ijarah we have explained. Translation: al-Qudūrī said: The will is not obligatory but is recommended. Qiyās rejects its permissibility because the will is a transfer of ownership deferred to the time of the cessation of his ownership. If this transfer were deferred to the time of its existence (i.e., while ownership still exists) in the manner that one says 'I make you owner tomorrow,' that is invalid; so this (the will) is even more (invalid). But we have made the will permissible, based on istiḥsān, due to the people's need for it. Because man is deceived by his hope and is deficient in his deeds. So when illness befalls him and he fears death, he needs to remedy what has preceded of his shortcomings through his wealth, in such a way that if he dies in that illness, his afterlife objective is achieved; and if health lifts him up, he will spend that wealth on his worldly objective. This objective is achieved in the legislation of the will, so we legislated it. And the like of it in ijarah we have explained. Explanation: The will is not obligatory; rather according to the author, it is recommended. And the requirement of qiyās is that the will should not be permissible at all, because the testator makes the beneficiary owner at a time when the testator himself is not owner. And if a person's ownership is still present but he defers the transfer to a future time and says 'I have made you owner of this thing tomorrow in the future,' this transfer is invalid, even though the ownership exists today and tomorrow. Despite that, it is declared invalid. So where ownership does not remain after death, it should be even more invalid. Nevertheless, the requirement of qiyās was that, but qiyās was abandoned and istiḥsān was acted upon, and it was declared permissible because people have need for it, just as people have need for ijarah, even though qiyās requires its non-permissibility, but based on istiḥsān, ijarah was permitted; similarly, the will was permitted. The reason for this is that man has hopes surrounding him, which cause him to commit many shortcomings. But when he falls into illness, he feels regret, so the Shariah permitted him to make up for the shortcomings related to his wealth that occurred due to the cycle of hopes. If he dies in that illness, his afterlife objective is fulfilled; and if he does not die, he can still use it for worldly benefits and derive benefit. And in the will, this same thing occurs, so the will was declared permissible.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage states the legal ruling of the will (al-waṣiyyah) and the reasoning behind it. The author (al-Qudūrī) declares that a will is not obligatory (wājib) but rather recommended (mustaḥabb). He then notes that pure analogy (qiyās) would actually reject its permissibility. Why? Because a will is a transfer of ownership (tamlīk) that is deferred (muḍāf) to a time after death, when the testator no longer possesses ownership. By analogy to a contract where someone says 'I make you owner tomorrow' while still owning the property—such a contract is invalid—a will, being deferred to a time when ownership has ceased, should be even more invalid. However, the Hanafi school sets aside this qiyās in favor of istiḥsān (juristic preference) based on the need of people. Human beings are often deceived by hopes and neglect their religious duties. When illness strikes and death threatens, they need to make up for past shortcomings by bequeathing their wealth. If they die, the bequest achieves its spiritual purpose; if they recover, they can use the property for their current needs. Just as the contract of ijarah (lease) is permitted by istiḥsān despite qiyās (since it involves prepayment for future benefit), so too is the will permitted.

Key Terms
وصیت (waṣiyyah): A transfer of ownership deferred to after death by way of gratuitous transfer.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning that would reject the validity of a will based on its deferred nature.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to need and public interest.
اجارہ (ijārah): A lease contract that is also permitted by istihsan despite qiyas.
تملیک مضاف (tamlīk muḍāf): A transfer of ownership that is deferred to a future time or event.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does qiyās (analogy) reject the permissibility of a will?
A) Because the will is a tamlīk muḍāf (deferred transfer) to a time after death, and even a deferred transfer to a future time while ownership still exists is invalid.
B) Because the will may involve an heir as beneficiary.
C) Because the testator might be in debt.
D) Because the bequest may exceed one-third of the estate.

Key Takeaway
A will is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib, and its validity is based on istihsan overriding qiyas due to human need, parallel to ijarah.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
Legal Ruling of Bequest: Mustahabb and Justified by Istihsan
Explains Hanafi ruling on bequest, rebuts opposition by qiyas, and provides proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequest (wasiyya) as mustahabb, explain why strict analogy (qiyas) opposes it, and justify the use of istihsan based on human need and textual evidence.

Core Idea
Bequest is mustahabb, not wajib, and is permitted by istihsan despite qiyas opposing.

In this passage, the author establishes that bequest (wasiyya) is a recommended act, not an obligatory one. He acknowledges that strict analogy (qiyas) would deem it invalid because ownership ends at death. However, the Hanafi school employs istihsan (juristic preference) to permit it due to human need and textual evidence. Let's unpack the reasoning and the proofs that support this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Locate the explicit statement that bequest is not wajib but mustahabb (recommended). Note that 'mustahabb' in Hanafi terminology corresponds to sunnah ghayr muakkadah.
The matn says 'الوصية غير واجبة وهي مستحبة'.
2
Understand the qiyas objection
Analogy (qiyas) opposes bequest because it is a transfer of ownership (tamlik) attached to a time after death, when the testator's ownership has ceased. Compare with the invalid case of saying 'I make you owner tomorrow' while still alive – even that is invalid, so a post-death transfer is even more problematic.
The illa (effective cause) is attaching ownership transfer to a time when the transferor does not own the property.
3
Apply istihsan
The Hanafi school abandons the qiyas ruling in favor of istihsan due to people's need (hajah). Humans often neglect spiritual duties, and bequest allows them to compensate. Istihsan overrides qiyas when there is a stronger equitable reason.
Ijarah (leasing) is another example where istihsan overrides qiyas.
4
Examine the proofs
The passage cites Quran (verse about bequest before inheritance), hadith (one-third charity), and consensus of the ummah (ijma) to support the validity of bequest. These provide textual authority.
Ownership after death remains for certain needs like shrouding and debt, countering the objection that ownership ceases entirely.
5
Note the qualification
Bequest is valid only up to one-third of the estate and only for a non-heir, without the permission of heirs. This limit prevents undue burden on heirs.
The text states 'تصح للاجنبي في الثلث من غير اجازة الورثة'.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد ۱۹
وصیت کی شرعی حیثیت
قال الوصية غير واجبة وهي مستحبة والقياس يابى جوازها لانه تملیک مضاف الى حال زوال مالكيته ولو اضيف الى حال قيامها بان قیل ملكتك غدا كان باطلا فهذا اولى الا انا استحسناه لحاجة الناس اليها فان الانسان مغرور بامله مقصر فى عمله فاذا عرض له المرض وخاف البيات يحتاج الى تلافي بعض ما فرط منه من التفريط بماله على وجه لو مضى فيه يتحقق مقصده المالى ولو انهضه البرء يصرفه الى مطلبه الحالي وفي شرع الوصية ذلك فشرعناه ومثله في الاجارة بيناه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ وصیت واجب نہیں مستحب ہے اور قیاس اس کے جواز کا انکار کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ وصیت ایسی تملیک ہے جو اس کی مالکیت کے زوال کے وقت کی جانب مضاف ہے اور اگر اس تملیک کی اضافت مالکیت کے قیام کے وقت کی جانب کی جائے اس طریقہ پر کہ کہا جائے میں نے تجھ کو کل مالک بنا دیا، تو یہ باطل ہے پس یہ بدرجہ اولیٰ مگر ہم نے وصیت کو بناء پر استحسان جائز قرار دیا ومیت کی جانب لوگوں کی حاجت کی وجہ سے اس لئے کہ انسان اپنی امید کی وجہ سے دھو کہ میں پڑ جاتا ہے اپنے عمل میں کوتاہی کر دیتا ہے پس جب اس کو مرض عارض ہو گیا اور وہ ہلاکت سے ڈرا تو وہ اس کو تا ہی کے تدارک کا محتاج ہوتا ہے جو اس کی جانب سے مقدم ہو چکی ہیں اپنے مال کے ذریعہ اس طریقہ پر کہ اگر وہ اس مرض میں مر گیا تو اس کا اخروی مقصد تحقیق ہو جائے گا اور اگر صحت نے اس کو اٹھا دیا تو وہ اس مال کو دنیوی مقصد میں صرف کرے گا اور وصیت کے مشروع کرنے میں یہ مقصد حاصل ہے تو اس کو ہم نے مشروع قرار دیا اور اسی کے مثل اجارہ میں ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں۔
تشریح وصیت واجب نہیں البتہ بقول مصنف مستحب ہے اور قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ وصیت جائز ہی نہ ہو۔ اس لئے کہ موصی موصی لہ کو ایسے وقت مالک بناتا ہے جب کہ موصی خود بھی مالک نہیں ہے، اور اگر کسی شخص کی ملکیت برقرار ہے مگر وہ ملکیت کی اضافت آئندہ زمانہ کی طرف کر دے اور یوں کہے کہ میں نے تجھے اس چیز کا کل آئندہ مالک بنا دیا تو یہ تملیک باطل ہے، حالانکہ ملک کی ملکیت آج بھی ہے اور کل بھی ، اس کے باوجود اسکو باطل قرار دیا گیا ہے۔
تو جہاں مرنے کے بعد ملکیت ہی نہیں رہتی وہ بدرجہ اولیٰ باطل ہونی چاہئے ۔ بہر حال قیاس کا تقاضہ تھا، لیکن قیاس کو چھوڑ کر استحسان پر عمل کیا گیا ہے اور اس کو جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے کیونکہ لوگوں کو اس کی حاجت ہے، جیسے لوگوں کو اجارہ کی حاجت ہے اگر چہ قیاس اس کے عدم جواز کا تقاضہ کرتا ہے مگر بناء پر استحسان جیسے اجارہ کو جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے ای طرح وصیت کو جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے۔
وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ انسان کو امیدوں نے گھیر رکھا ہے جس کی وجہ سے وہ بہت سی کوتاہیاں کر دیتا ہے لیکن جب مرض میں پھنسا تو اب اس کو ندامت ہوئی تو شریعت نے اس کو اجازت دی کہ امیدوں کے چکر میں مال کے متعلق جو کوتاہیاں صادر ہوئی ہیں ان کی تلافی کر دے ، اگر وہ اس مرض میں مرجائے تو اخروی مقصد پورا ہو جائے اور اگر نہ مرے تو دینوی مقاصد میں ابھی اس کو استعمال کر کے فائدہ اٹھائے ۔
اور وصیت کے اندر بھی یہی ہوتا ہے اس وجہ سے وصیت کو جائز قرار دیا گیا ہے۔

وقد تبقى المالكية بعد الموت باعتبار الحاجة كما في قدر التجهيز والدين وقد نطق به الكتاب وهو قول الله تعالى من بعد وصية يوصى بها او دين والسنة وهو قول النبي عليه السلام ان الله تعالى تصدق عليكم بثلث اموالكم فى اخرا عماركم زيادة لكم فى اعمالكم تضعونها حيث شئتم اوقال حيث اجبتم وعليه اجماع الامة ثم تصح للاجنبي في الثلث من غير اجازة الورثة لماروينا وسنبين ما هو الافضل فيه ان شاء الله تعالى
ترجمہ اور ملکیت باقی رہتی ہے موت کے بعد حاجت کے اعتبار سے جیسے تجہیز اور قرض کی مقدار میں اور کتاب اللہ اس کے جواز کے متعلق ناطق ہے اور وہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا فرمان ہے، من بعد وصية يوصى بها اودین اور اس کے جواز کے متعلق سنت ناطق ہے اور دو نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہارے اوپر تمہاری آخری عمروں میں تمہارے ثلث مال کا صدقہ کر دیا تمہارے اعمال کی زیادتی کی غرض سے جہاں تم چاہو اس کو خرچ کر دیا فرمایا، حیث اجبتُم اور جواز وصیت کے او پر اجماع منعقد ہو چکا ہے پھر وصیت صحیح ہے اجنبی کے لئے ثلث کے اندر ورثہ کی اجازت کے بغیر اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں اور ہم عنقریب بیان کریں گے اس طریقہ کو جو وصیت کے سلسلہ میں افضل ہے اگر چاہا اللہ تعالیٰ نے ۔
تشریح اور قیاس کی دلیل میں جو یہ کہا گیا کہ موصی کی موت کے بعد اس کی حاجت و مالکیت باقی نہیں رہتی تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ جتنی میت کو ضرورت ہے وہاں تک میت کی مالکیت باقی رہتی ہے اسی وجہ سے تجہیز و تکفین اور ا داودین کو سب سے مقدم رکھا جاتا ہے کیونکہ اس میں میت کی ضرورت ہے ( وبیناه في درس السراجی)۔
اور قران وحدیث سے وصیت کا جواز ثابت ہے۔
فرمان باری ہے ، فان كان له خوةً فَلا مَهِ السلاسُ مِن بَعدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصى بها أود ین یعنی اگر میت کے ( دو یا اس سے زیادہ ) بھائی ہیں تو اس کی ماں کے لئے چھٹا حصہ کے بعد وصیت یا بعد اداء قرض ) یعنی جس قدر وارثوں کے حصے گزر چکے ہیں یہ سب میت کی وصیت اور اس کے قرض کو جدا کر لینے کے بعد وارثوں کو دئے جائیں گے اور وارثوں کا مال وہ بقیہ ہو گا جو مقدار وصیت و قرض کے نکال لینے کے بعد باقی رہے گا اور نصف اور ثلث وغیرہ اسی مابقی کا مراد ہے نہ تمام مال کا۔ اسی طرح حدیث سے بھی وصیت کا جواز ثابت ہے جو حدیث متن میں مذکور ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہارے اموال کا ثلث تم پر صدقہ کر دیا جب کہ آپ کی زندگی کے آخری لمحات آئیں تا کہ اس مال کی بدولت تمہارے اعمال میں اضافہ ہو سکے اور تم اپنی دینی ضروریات میں جہاں چاہو اس کو خرچ کر سکو، یہاں ایک روایت میں یہ الفاظ ہیں ، تضعو نھا حيث شنتم اور ایک میں یہ الفاظ ہیں حیث اجبتم اور جواز وصیت پر امت کا جماع ہے۔ پھر ثاث مال میں جواز وصیت کے لئے ورثہ کی اجازت درکار نہیں ہے جب کہ وصیت کسی وارثت کے لئے نہ ہو بلکہ کسی اجنبی کے
متنبیه - وصیت کی چار قسمیں ہیں:
Book of Bequests. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, vol. 19. Legal status of bequest. He said: Bequest is not obligatory, it is recommended. Analogy refuses its permissibility because it is a transfer of ownership attached to a time of the cessation of his ownership. If it were attached to a time of its existence, by saying 'I make you owner tomorrow,' it would be invalid, so this is more so. But we approved it by istihsan due to people's need for it. For man is deceived by his hope and negligent in his actions. When illness strikes him and he fears death, he needs to make up for some of his negligence regarding his wealth in a way that if he dies in it, his intended religious purpose is achieved, and if he recovers, he spends it for his current goal. In the legislation of bequest this is achieved, so we legislated it. Its like in ijarah we explained. Translation: Al-Quduri said that bequest is not obligatory, it is recommended. Analogy refuses its permissibility... [Continued with Urdu commentary]. And ownership remains after death due to need, as in the amount for shrouding and debt. The Book has spoken of it: 'After a bequest he makes or a debt.' The Sunnah is the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Allah has given you in charity one-third of your wealth at the end of your lives to increase your deeds; you place it wherever you wish' or 'wherever you wish.' And upon this is the consensus of the ummah. Then it is valid for a non-heir within one-third without the permission of the heirs, due to what we narrated, and we will soon explain what is best in it, insha'Allah. [Continued with Urdu commentary and elaboration].
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the legal status of bequest (wasiyya) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by stating the ruling: bequest is not wajib but mustahabb (recommended). The author, Al-Quduri, acknowledges that strict analogy (qiyas) would oppose its permissibility because a bequest is a transfer of ownership (tamlik) that takes effect after death, at a time when the testator's ownership has ceased. If someone were to say 'I make you owner tomorrow' while still alive, that transfer would be invalid, so a post-death transfer is even more problematic. However, the Hanafi school abandons this analogy in favor of istihsan (juristic preference) due to people's need for bequests. Human beings are often negligent about spiritual obligations, and when they fall ill, they feel regret. Bequest allows them to make up for some shortcomings by dedicating wealth to good causes. If they die, the bequest fulfills their religious goal; if they recover, they can use the wealth for worldly purposes. This is analogous to ijarah (leasing), which is also permitted by istihsan despite qiyas opposing it. The passage then provides counterarguments: ownership after death does remain for certain needs like shrouding and debt repayment. Textual evidence from the Quran (verse about bequest before inheritance distribution) and the hadith (one-third charity) support bequest, and there is consensus (ijma) of the ummah. Finally, it clarifies that bequest is valid for a non-heir within one-third without heirs' permission.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyya): A voluntary transfer of ownership of property to another after the testator's death
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that abandons strict analogy in favor of a more equitable ruling due to need

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, why does strict analogy (qiyas) oppose the validity of a bequest (wasiyya)?
A) Because the testator's ownership ceases at death.
B) Because bequests are considered wasteful.
C) Because the heirs' rights are infringed.
D) Because the Prophet prohibited bequests.

Key Takeaway
Bequest is a recommended act (mustahabb) validated by istihsan due to human need, despite qiyas opposing it, and limited to one-third of the estate for non-heirs.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
Bequest (Wasiyyah): Proofs and the Principle of Remaining Ownership After Death
Establishes bequest's permissibility via Quran, Sunnah, ijma, and rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four proofs (qiyas, Quran, Sunnah, ijma) for the validity of wasiyyah and explain the Hanafi principle that ownership continues after death for essential needs.

Core Idea
Ownership does not cease at death; it remains for the deceased's essential needs, allowing bequest up to one-third without heirs' permission.

Death typically ends legal ownership, but Hanafi fiqh recognizes that certain needs persist after death—such as shrouding, burial expenses, and debt clearance. This reality grounds the validity of bequest (wasiyyah) as a means to address those needs and increase one's deeds. In this lesson, we explore how the author of Al-Hidayah marshals rational argument, Quranic verses, prophetic hadith, and unanimous consensus to prove that bequest is permissible and that the deceased retains a limited ownership for these purposes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What legal act is being discussed? What is its hukm level (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.)? The passage focuses on permissibility (jawaz) of bequest, but the Hanafi position is that it is sunnah mustahabbah (recommended) unless it involves an overdue religious duty (in which case it becomes wajib).
The base ruling is permissibility within one-third for a non-heir.
2
Locate the rational proof (qiyas)
Identify the qiyas argument: the living owner fully owns and can dispose; the deceased has a limited ownership for needs (shroud, debt). Find the illa (effective cause): need (hajah). Understand the objector's claim that ownership ends at death, and the Hanafi response that without continued ownership, shroud and debt would not be payable.
This qiyas is khafiy (hidden analogy) because the need is not apparent.
3
Examine the naqli proofs: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma
Read the Quranic reference (4:12: 'after a bequest...') and the hadith about one-third being a charity at the end of life. Note that the hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) yet sufficient for permissibility. Observe that the author also cites ijma (consensus) of the Ummah.
The hadith wording: 'Allah has given you in charity one-third of your wealth... you put it wherever you wish.'
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah of the dalils
How does each dalil prove the ruling? The Quranic phrase 'after a bequest' implies bequest is executed before inheritance, hence valid. The hadith explicitly permits one-third. The qiyas shows continuity of ownership for needs. Ijma confirms the entire structure.
The strength of the evidence supports the ruling as sunnah, not fard, because the commands are permissive, not obligatory.
5
State the practical ruling and its parameters
Conclude: a bequest to a non-heir (ajnabi) is valid up to one-third of the estate without the permission of the heirs. If the bequest exceeds one-third, it requires heirs' consent. This ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.
The one-third is calculated from the total estate after debts and funeral expenses.

كتاب الوصايا
وقد تبقى المالكية بعد الموت باعتبار الحاجة كما في قدر التجهيز والدين وقد نطق به الكتاب وهو قول الله تعالى من بعد وصية يوصى بها او دين والسنة وهو قول النبي عليه السلام ان الله تعالى تصدق عليكم بثلث اموالكم فى اخرا عماركم زيادة لكم فى اعمالكم تضعونها حيث شئتم اوقال حيث اجبتم وعليه اجماع الامة ثم تصح للاجنبي في الثلث من غير اجازة الورثة لماروينا وسنبين ما هو الافضل فيه ان شاء الله تعالى ترجمہ اور ملکیت باقی رہتی ہے موت کے بعد حاجت کے اعتبار سے جیسے تجہیز اور قرض کی مقدار میں اور کتاب اللہ اس کے جواز کے متعلق ناطق ہے اور وہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا فرمان ہے، من بعد وصية يوصى بها اودین اور اس کے جواز کے متعلق سنت ناطق ہے اور دو نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہارے اوپر تمہاری آخری عمروں میں تمہارے ثلث مال کا صدقہ کر دیا تمہارے اعمال کی زیادتی کی غرض سے جہاں تم چاہو اس کو خرچ کر دیا فرمایا، حیث اجبتُم اور جواز وصیت کے او پر اجماع منعقد ہو چکا ہے پھر وصیت صحیح ہے اجنبی کے لئے ثلث کے اندر ورثہ کی اجازت کے بغیر اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جس کو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں اور ہم عنقریب بیان کریں گے اس طریقہ کو جو وصیت کے سلسلہ میں افضل ہے اگر چاہا اللہ تعالیٰ نے ۔
تشریح اور قیاس کی دلیل میں جو یہ کہا گیا کہ موصی کی موت کے بعد اس کی حاجت و مالکیت باقی نہیں رہتی تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ جتنی میت کو ضرورت ہے وہاں تک میت کی مالکیت باقی رہتی ہے اسی وجہ سے تجہیز و تکفین اور ا داودین کو سب سے مقدم رکھا جاتا ہے کیونکہ اس میں میت کی ضرورت ہے ( وبیناه في درس السراجی)۔
اور قران وحدیث سے وصیت کا جواز ثابت ہے۔
فرمان باری ہے ، فان كان له خوةً فَلا مَهِ السلاسُ مِن بَعدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصى بها أود ین یعنی اگر میت کے ( دو یا اس سے زیادہ ) بھائی ہیں تو اس کی ماں کے لئے چھٹا حصہ کے بعد وصیت یا بعد اداء قرض ) یعنی جس قدر وارثوں کے حصے گزر چکے ہیں یہ سب میت کی وصیت اور اس کے قرض کو جدا کر لینے کے بعد وارثوں کو دئے جائیں گے اور وارثوں کا مال وہ بقیہ ہو گا جو مقدار وصیت و قرض کے نکال لینے کے بعد باقی رہے گا اور نصف اور ثلث وغیرہ اسی مابقی کا مراد ہے نہ تمام مال کا۔ اسی طرح حدیث سے بھی وصیت کا جواز ثابت ہے جو حدیث متن میں مذکور ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہارے اموال کا ثلث تم پر صدقہ کر دیا جب کہ آپ کی زندگی کے آخری لمحات آئیں تا کہ اس مال کی بدولت تمہارے اعمال میں اضافہ ہو سکے اور تم اپنی دینی ضروریات میں جہاں چاہو اس کو خرچ کر سکو، یہاں ایک روایت میں یہ الفاظ ہیں ، تضعو نھا حيث شنتم اور ایک میں یہ الفاظ ہیں حیث اجبتم اور جواز وصیت پر امت کا جماع ہے۔ پھر ثلث مال میں جواز وصیت کے لئے ورثہ کی اجازت درکار نہیں ہے جب کہ وصیت کسی وارثت کے لئے نہ ہو بلکہ کسی اجنبی کے
Rational Proof. The Book of Wills. And ownership remains after death considering need, like the amount for shroud and debt. The Book has spoken of it: the saying of Allah Almighty: 'after a bequest which he bequeaths or a debt'. And the Sunnah: the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Indeed Allah Almighty has given you in charity one-third of your wealth at the end of your lives, as an increase for you in your deeds, you put it wherever you wish' or he said 'wherever you desire'. And upon it is the consensus of the Ummah. Then it is valid for a non-heir within the one-third without permission of the heirs, due to what we have narrated, and we will explain what is better in it, if Allah wills. Translation: And ownership remains after death considering need, like the amount for shroud and debt. The Book of Allah speaks of its permissibility: the command of Allah Almighty: 'after a bequest which he bequeaths or a debt'. And the Sunnah speaks of its permissibility: the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him, that Allah Almighty has given you in charity one-third of your wealth in your last ages for the increase of your deeds, you spend it where you wish. He said: 'where you desire'. And consensus has been established on the permissibility of bequest. Then the bequest is valid for a non-heir within the one-third without the permission of the heirs, due to the hadith we have narrated, and we will soon explain that which is better regarding bequest, if Allah wills. Explanation: And regarding the rational proof, what was said that after the testator's death his need and ownership do not remain, so the answer is given that to the extent of the deceased's necessity, ownership remains. For this reason, shrouding and burial expenses and debts are given precedence because therein is the need of the deceased (and we have explained it in Dars al-Siraji). And the permissibility of bequest is proven from Quran and Hadith. The command of Allah is: '...if he has brothers, then for his mother a sixth, after a bequest which he bequeaths or a debt.' That is, if the deceased has (two or more) brothers, then for his mother one-sixth after bequest or after payment of debt. That is, all the shares of heirs are given after separating the deceased's bequest and his debt. And the heirs' wealth is the remainder after extracting the amount of bequest and debt. And half and one-third etc. refer to this remainder, not the entire wealth. Similarly, the permissibility of bequest is proven from hadith, which is mentioned in the matn. Its meaning is that Allah Almighty has given you one-third of your wealth in charity when the last moments of your life come, so that by means of this wealth your deeds may increase, and you may spend it in your religious needs wherever you wish. Here, in one narration the words are 'tada'unaha haythu shi'tum' and in another 'haythu ajabtum'. And there is consensus of the Ummah on the permissibility of bequest. Then, for the permissibility of bequest within the one-third, the permission of the heirs is not required when the bequest is not for an heir but for a non-heir.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of bequests (wasiyyah) and the continued ownership of the deceased for certain needs. The text begins by stating a rational justification: ownership does not entirely cease at death; it remains to the extent of necessity, such as the expenses for shrouding and burial (tajhiz wa takfin) and debts. This is supported by Quranic verses (e.g., 4:12: 'after a bequest which he bequeaths or a debt') and the hadith in which the Prophet said that Allah has given the right to bequeath one-third of one's wealth as a charity at the end of life. The passage also cites ijma' (consensus) on the validity of bequests. Importantly, a bequest to a non-heir is valid without the heirs' permission as long as it is within one-third of the estate. The commentary then explains that the rational objection (that ownership ends at death) is answered by the fact that the deceased's needs (shroud and debt) require that some ownership remains; hence these expenses are prioritized over inheritance. The Quranic verse quoted is interpreted to mean that the shares of inheritance are calculated after deducting bequests and debts. The hadith text is elaborated: the one-third is a divine gift to increase one's deeds during the terminal illness. The passage concludes that no permission from heirs is needed for a bequest to a non-heir within the one-third.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): A legal disposition by a person on his deathbed regarding his property after death, binding only up to one-third unless heirs consent.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum a testator may bequeath to non-heirs without heirs' permission.
اجنبي (ajnabi): A person who is not a legal heir (i.e., not entitled to inheritance from the deceased).
حاجة (hajah): Need, the effective cause (illa) for continued ownership after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the deceased still needs the property for his own use in the grave.
B) Because of the need for shrouding and burial expenses and debt.
C) Because the heirs have no rights until after bequest is executed.
D) Because bequest is obligatory upon every Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a non-heir within one-third of the estate is valid without heirs' permission, based on Quran, Sunnah, ijma, and rational proof that ownership continues after death for essential needs.

Classification of Bequest Types in Hanafi Fiqh
Lists the four categories of bequest rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four legal categories of bequest (wajib, makruh, mubah, mustahabb) and state the condition that triggers each classification.

Core Idea
A bequest is not always recommended — it can be obligatory, disliked, permissible, or recommended depending on the testator's circumstances.

This passage from the Hanafi tradition presents a concise classification of bequests (wasiyyah) into four distinct legal rulings. It highlights that the ruling on a bequest depends on the testator's situation, particularly regarding overdue religious obligations and the testator's character. Understanding this classification helps ensure that bequests are made in accordance with Islamic law and the testator's duties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories
List the four rulings mentioned: wajib, makruh, mubah, mustahabb.
Each category corresponds to a different scenario of the testator.
2
Understand when a bequest is wajib
A bequest becomes wajib when the testator has unpaid religious obligations such as zakat or kaffarat that must be fulfilled from the estate.
This is an obligation upon the testator's estate, not a voluntary act.
3
Understand when a bequest is makruh
A bequest is makruh if the testator is a habitual sinner (fasiq/fajir), as such a person may use the property for sinful purposes.
The dislike is connected to the character of the testator, not the act itself.
4
Distinguish mubah from mustahabb
A bequest is mubah for a wealthy person who has no outstanding obligations, and mustahabb in all other cases where no invalidating factor exists.
The default status is mustahabb (recommended) unless a specific condition changes it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متنبیہ - وصیت کی چار قسمیں ہیں:۔
واجب جیسے زکوۃ و کفارات کے حق میں۔ مکروہ فساق و فجار کے لئے۔
-- مباح مال دار کے لئے ۔
-۴- اور ان کے علاوہ میں اگر کوئی عارضِ مُبطل نہ ہو تو مستحب ہے۔ تفصیل کے لئے دیکھئے شامی ص ۴۱۵، ج ۵-
Note: Four types of bequest: Wajib (obligatory) - like regarding zakat and expiations. Makruh (disliked) - for sinners and immoral people. Mubah (permissible) - for a wealthy person. And (fourth) besides these, if there is no invalidating impediment, then Mustahabb (recommended). For detail, see Shami, vol. 5, p. 415.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This is a brief note (tanbih) categorizing bequests into four legal rulings. First, a bequest can be wajib (obligatory) when the testator has unpaid religious obligations like zakat (poor-due) or kaffarat (expiations) that must be fulfilled from the estate. Second, it is makruh (disliked) if the testator is a habitual sinner or immoral person (fasiq/fajir), as his bequest may be to support sinful activities. Third, it is mubah (permissible) for a wealthy person (mal-dar) who has no religious obligations to meet. Fourth, in all other cases where no invalidating factor exists, bequest is mustahabb (recommended) as a means of earning reward. The author refers for detail to Shami (Ibn Abidin's Radd al-Muhtar), a standard Hanafi reference.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligatory category of bequest, such as when the testator owes zakat or kaffarat that must be paid from his estate.
مکروہ (makruh): A disliked bequest, e.g., by a sinner who is likely to misuse the property, or bequeathing to sinful purposes.
مباح (mubah): A permissible bequest, for a wealthy person who has no outstanding obligations.
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended bequest, in all cases where no invalidating impediment exists and no other category applies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When made to a non-heir
B) When made during a terminal illness
C) When it involves zakat or kaffarat obligations
D) When the testator is wealthy

Key Takeaway
The ruling on a bequest varies from wajib to mustahabb depending on the testator's obligations, character, and wealth.

The One-Third Limit on Bequests: Evidence and Rationale
Ruling with proof on one-third limit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequests exceeding one-third, cite the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas as evidence, and explain the rationale based on the testator's independence from wealth.

Core Idea
A bequest beyond one-third is invalid; the Prophet set one-third as the maximum to protect heirs' rights.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the well-known rule that a bequest cannot exceed one-third of the estate. The author presents the proof from the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, where the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) rejected bequests of the whole or half and permitted only one-third. The passage also provides a rational basis: upon nearing death, the testator becomes independent of wealth, and the heirs' right attaches to the estate. Shari'ah allowed one-third for non-heirs to compensate for the testator's possible negligence in charity during life, but fully protects the heirs' share.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its implications
State the Hanafi ruling: bequests exceeding one-third are invalid (la tajuz) and constitute hayf (injustice), a major sin. The excess is void unless heirs consent after death.
The ruling applies to bequests to non-heirs; bequests to heirs are also hayf and invalid without consent.
2
Locate the primary proof
Recognize the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas as the dalil. The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) first negated bequests of the whole and half, then permitted one-third, saying 'الثلث والثلث كثير' (one-third, and one-third is much).
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted by all schools.
3
Understand the ta'lil (rationale)
The testator becomes mustaghni 'an al-mal (independent of wealth) upon nearing death. This independence necessitates that the heirs' right becomes attached to the estate. Shari'ah permitted up to one-third for non-heirs to allow the testator to make up for deficiencies in charity during life, but fully protected the heirs' right to the remaining two-thirds.
The rationale is based on the principle that the deceased no longer needs the wealth, so it should pass to those who have a right.
4
Distinguish between bequests to heirs and non-heirs
A bequest to an heir is also considered hayf because it disrupts the fixed shares ordained by Allah. It is invalid unless all other heirs consent after death.
The passage quotes the hadith: 'al-hayf fi al-wasiyyati min akbar al-kaba'ir.'
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
If a testator leaves a bequest of more than one-third to a non-heir, the excess is automatically invalid and becomes part of the residue for the heirs. If the heirs consent after death, the excess can be enforced.
Consent must be given after death to be valid; pre-mortem consent is not sufficient.

Source Text

قال ولا تجوز بما زاد على الثلث لقول النبي عليه السلام في حديث سعد بن ابی وقاص رضى الله عنه الثلث والثلث كثير بعد ما نفى وصيته بالكل والنصف ولانه حق الورثة وهذا لانه انعقد سبب الزوال اليهم وهو استغناؤه عن المال فاوجب تعلق حقهم به الا ان الشرع لم يظهره فى حق الاجانب بقدر الثلث ليتدارك تقصیره على ما بيناه واظهره فى حق الورثة لان الظاهر انه لا يتصدق به عليهم تحرزا عما يتفق من الايثار على ما نبينه وقد جاء في الحديث الحيف في الوصية من اكبر الكبائر وفسروه بالزيادة على الثلث وبالوصية للوارث
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور وصیت جائز نہیں ہے اس مقدار کے ساتھ جو ٹکٹ پر زیادہ ہو نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کے فرمان کی وجہ سے سعد بن ابی وقاص رضی عنہ اللہ کی حدیث میں پر تہائی تک اور تہائی زیادہ ہے، یہ اس کے بعد فرمایا تھا جب کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم ان کی کل اور نصف کی وصیت کی نفی فرما چکے تھے اور اس لئے کہ مال ورثہ کا حق ہے اور یہ اس لئے کہ ورثہ کی جانب زوال کا سبب منعقد ہو چکا ہے اور وہ سبب موصی کا مال سے مستغنی ہوتا ہے یہ استغناء اس مال کے ساتھ ان کا حق متعلق ہونے کو ثابت کرے گا مگر شریعت نے تہائی مقدار میں اجانب کے حق میں اس استغناء کو ظاہر نہیں کیا تا کہ ہمارے مذکورہ بیان کے مطابق موصی کی کوتاہی کا تدارک ہو سکے اور ورثہ کے حق میں استغناء کو ظاہر کیا ہے اس لئے کہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ موصی ثلث کا ورثہ پر صدقہ نہیں کرے گا احتراز کرتے ہوئے اس ایثار سے جو اتفاقا واقع ہورہا ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کریں گے اور حدیث میں آیا ہے کہ وصیت کے اندر ظلم اکبر الکبائر میں سے ہے اور علماء نے حیف کی تفسیر ثلث سے زیادہ اور وارث کے لئے وصیت سے کی ہے۔
تشریح مریض موت کا حق تنہائی مال تک ہے لہذا ایک تہائی تک وہ تصرف کر سکتا ہے اس سے زیادہ میں وصیت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ حدیث میں حضرت سعد بن ابی وقاص رضی اللہ عنہ کا تفصیلی واقعہ موجود ہے جس میں آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پورے مال کی وصیر سے اور نصف کی وصیت سے منع فرمایا تھا بس ٹکٹ کے اندر وصیت کرنے کی اجازت دی تھی اور ساتھ ہی یہ بھی یہ فرمایا تھا کہ ایسے ثلث بھی
زیادہ ہے۔
پھر جب مالک ( مریض موت ) اس مرحلہ پر پہنچ گیا تو اب وہ مال سے مستغنی ہو گیا اور اس کا مال سے مستغنی ہونا اس بات کو واجب کرتا ہے کہ اس مال کے ساتھ اس کے ورثہ کا حق متعلق ہو جائے لہذا اس مال کے ساتھ ورثہ کا حق متعلق ہو گیا اور ایسا سبب منعقد ہو گیا کہ
He (al-Quduri) said: And it is not valid for more than one-third, due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (may Allah be pleased with him): 'One-third, and one-third is much,' after he negated bequest of the whole and half. And because it is the right of the heirs. And this is because the cause of transfer to them has been established, which is his independence from wealth, so it necessitated the attachment of their right to it. However, the Law did not manifest this in respect of non-heirs up to one-third, to compensate for his deficiency as we explained, and manifested it in respect of the heirs because the apparent is that he will not give it in charity to them, avoiding the preference (i'tihar) that may occur, as we will explain. And it has come in the hadith: 'Injustice (hayf) in bequest is among the major sins.' And they interpreted it as exceeding one-third and making a bequest to an heir. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And bequest is not valid with that which exceeds one-third, due to the command of the Prophet in the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas: 'Up to one-third, and one-third is much.' This he said after he had negated bequest of the whole and half. And because the wealth is the right of the heirs. And this is because the cause of transfer to them has been established, and that cause is the testator's independence from wealth. This independence proves the attachment of their right to this wealth. But the Law did not manifest this independence for non-heirs up to one-third, so that the testator's deficiency could be remedied as per our explanation, and manifested it for the heirs because the apparent is that the testator will not give one-third in charity to them, avoiding any incidental preference, according to the detail we will explain. And in the hadith: 'Injustice in bequest is among the major sins.' And scholars interpreted 'injustice' as exceeding the third and bequest to an heir. Explanation: The terminally ill person's right is over his wealth up to one-third; thus he may dispose up to one-third. Bequeathing more than that is invalid. Because in the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, the Prophet forbade bequest of the entire wealth and half, and only permitted bequest within one-third, saying 'one-third is also much.' Then when the owner (terminally ill) reaches this stage, he becomes independent of wealth, and his independence necessitates that the right of his heirs becomes attached to the wealth. Thus the right of the heirs is attached, and a cause is established that...
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the limitation of bequest to one-third. The text begins with al-Quduri's statement: 'It is not valid for more than one-third.' The proof is the famous hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, where the Prophet initially rejected bequest of the whole or half, and then allowed one-third, saying 'one-third is also much.' The rational basis (ta'lil) is that upon approaching death, the testator becomes 'independent of wealth' (mustaghni 'an al-mal), meaning he will no longer need it, so the right of the heirs becomes attached to the estate. However, Shari'ah did not manifest this attachment fully against non-heirs; it allowed up to one-third to be given to non-heirs to compensate for the testator's possible negligence in charitable acts during his life. In contrast, the right of heirs is fully manifested because it is not common for a person to give charity to his own heirs (they will inherit anyway). The text also cites the hadith that 'hayf' (injustice) in bequest is among the major sins, and scholars interpret this as exceeding one-third or bequeathing to an heir (who already has a fixed share). The commentary elaborates on Sa'd's story: the Prophet forbade full and half, then permitted one-third, deeming even one-third large. It reiterates the reasoning: the testator's independence from wealth triggers the heirs' right, so they cannot be deprived of more than two-thirds without their consent.

Key Terms
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum permissible amount for bequests to non-heirs without heirs' consent.
حيف (hayf): Injustice or transgression in bequest, interpreted as exceeding one-third or bequeathing to an heir (which violates the heir's rightful share).
وارث (warith): An heir who is legally entitled to a share of the deceased's estate under the law of inheritance (fara'id).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Obligatory

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a bequest is limited to one-third of the estate; exceeding this is invalid and sinful unless heirs consent after death.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
The One-Third Limit on Bequests
Explains the prohibition of bequeathing more than one-third with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maximum permissible fraction for a bequest to a non-heir, derive the prohibition from the hadith, and apply the rule to scenarios involving bequests to heirs or exceeding one-third.

Core Idea
A bequest exceeding one-third is prohibited; the estate belongs to the heirs by right.

This lesson addresses a fundamental rule in Islamic inheritance and wills: a testator may only bequeath up to one-third of his estate to non-heirs. The ruling is firmly based on the Prophet's instruction to Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and is designed to balance the testator's desire for charity with the rights of legal heirs. We will examine the primary proof, the underlying rationale, and the two forms of prohibited transgression (hayf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what legal act is being discussed (a bequest/wasiyyah) and what hukm level applies. The text states that bequests exceeding one-third are not valid (la tujuz), implying prohibition (haram).
Also note that bequeathing to an heir is prohibited even within one-third.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the specific evidence cited. The text quotes the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas in which the Prophet said 'One-third, and one-third is a lot.' This is the primary textual proof.
The hadith is ahad (solitary) but accepted by the school as authoritative.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The Prophet's statement 'is a lot' indicates disapproval and restriction; combined with his previous negation of half and all, it establishes one-third as the maximum.
The imperative form is understood as a prohibition (tahrim).
4
Understand the rationale (right of heirs)
The text explains that upon approaching death, the testator becomes detached from wealth, causing the heirs' right to attach. The Law permits one-third for non-heirs to compensate for shortcomings, but bequests to heirs would cause unfair preference.
This rationale is based on the principles of justice and preventing harm.
5
Identify the two forms of hayf (transgression)
The hadith classifies 'transgression in the will' as a major sin. Scholars interpret hayf as (1) exceeding one-third and (2) bequeathing to an heir. Both are prohibited.
This step consolidates the practical applications of the ruling.

میت اپنے کتنے مال تک کسی کو وصیت کر سکتا ہے
قال ولا تجوز بما زاد على الثلث لقول النبي عليه السلام في حديث سعد بن ابی وقاص رضى الله عنه الثلث والثلث كثير بعد ما نفى وصيته بالكل والنصف ولانه حق الورثة وهذا لانه انعقد سبب الزوال اليهم وهو استغناؤه عن المال فاوجب تعلق حقهم به الا ان الشرع لم يظهره فى حق الاجانب بقدر الثلث ليتدارك تقصیره على ما بيناه واظهره فى حق الورثة لان الظاهر انه لا يتصدق به عليهم تحرزا عما يتفق من الايثار على ما نبينه وقد جاء في الحديث الحيف في الوصية من اكبر الكبائر وفسروه بالزيادة على الثلث وبالوصية للوارث

تشریح مریض موت کا حق تنہائی مال تک ہے لہذا ایک تہائی تک وہ تصرف کر سکتا ہے اس سے زیادہ میں وصیت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ حدیث میں حضرت سعد بن ابی وقاص رضی اللہ عنہ کا تفصیلی واقعہ موجود ہے جس میں آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے پورے مال کی وصیر سے اور نصف کی وصیت سے منع فرمایا تھا بس ٹکٹ کے اندر وصیت کرنے کی اجازت دی تھی اور ساتھ ہی یہ بھی یہ فرمایا تھا کہ ایسے ثلث بھی
زیادہ ہے۔
پھر جب مالک ( مریض موت ) اس مرحلہ پر پہنچ گیا تو اب وہ مال سے مستغنی ہو گیا اور اس کا مال سے مستغنی ہونا اس بات کو واجب کرتا ہے کہ اس مال کے ساتھ اس کے ورثہ کا حق متعلق ہو جائے لہذا اس مال کے ساتھ ورثہ کا حق متعلق ہو گیا اور ایسا سبب منعقد ہو گیا کہ یہ مال ورثہ کی جانب منتقل ہو جائے ۔
ورثہ کے حق کا اس مال کے ساتھ تعلق اس بات کو مقتضی ہے کہ تہائی کے اندر بھی اس کا تصرف نافذ نہ ہوگر ای دلیل بزرکور کی وجہ سے اس . جانب کے حق میں تصرف وصیت کی اجازت دے دی گئی تا کہ اصل مالک کی جانب سے متحقق ہونے والی تقصیر دیت کا تدارک ہو سکے۔ لہذا ہم نے موصی کے استغناء کو مقدار ثلث میں اجانب کے حق میں ظاہر نہیں کیا۔
البتہ اگر ورثہ میں سے کسی کے لئے وصیت کرتا ہے تو پھر یہ استغناء ظاہر ہوگا اور اس کا یہ تصرف نافذ نہ ہوگا۔
ورنہ یہاں بعض ورثہ کی تازی لازم آئے گی کیونکہ جب مورث بعض ورثہ کو وصیت کرے گا اور بعض کو نہ کرے گا تو بعض کو بعض پر ترجیح دے گا جو بعض کی تازی اور تکلیف کا سبب بنے گا تو اس صورت میں اتفاق ایسا ہوتا ہے کہ ایثار لازم آتا ہے لہذا اس کو سرے ہی سے نا جائز قرار دیا۔ اور حدیث کے اندر فرمایا گیا ہے کہ حیف اکبر الکبائر میں سے ہے یعنی بہت بڑا پاپ ہے۔
اور حیف کی تفسیر یہ ہے کہ تہائی سے زیادہ کی وصیت کرے یا وارث کے لئے وصیت کرے۔
To what extent may a dying person bequeath to someone? He (al-Quduri) said: A bequest is not valid for more than one-third, because of the saying of the Prophet ﷺ in the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas رضي الله عنه: 'One-third, and one-third is a lot,' after he had negated his will for the whole and for the half. And because it is the right of the heirs. And this is because the cause of transfer to them has been established, which is his dispensation from wealth, thus it necessitated the attachment of their right to it. However, the Law did not manifest this (dispensation) with respect to non-heirs to the extent of one-third, to compensate for his shortcoming as we explained. And it manifested it with respect to the heirs, because the apparent is that he does not give charity of one-third to them, avoiding any preference that may occur, as we will explain. And it has come in the hadith: 'Transgression in the will is among the major sins.' And they interpreted transgression as exceeding one-third and bequeathing to an heir. Translation: Al-Quduri said: A will is not valid for an amount that exceeds one-third, due to the command of the Prophet ﷺ in the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas رضي الله عنه: 'One-third, and one-third is a lot.' This was after he had prohibited him from bequeathing all and half. And because the wealth is the right of the heirs. And this is because the cause of transfer to the heirs has been established, and that cause is the testator's dispensation from the wealth. This dispensation necessitates that their right is attached to the wealth, but the Law did not manifest this dispensation with respect to non-heirs to the extent of one-third, so that the testator's shortcoming may be compensated as per our earlier statement. And it manifested the dispensation with respect to the heirs, because it is apparent that the testator will not give charity of one-third to them, avoiding any preference that may occur, as per the detail we will mention. And the hadith states: 'Transgression in the will is among the major sins,' and the scholars interpreted transgression as exceeding one-third and bequeathing to an heir. Explanation: The right of the deathly ill person is only to one-third of the wealth. Therefore, he can dispose of up to one-third. Bequeathing more than that is not valid, because of the detailed incident of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas رضي الله عنه in which the Prophet ﷺ prohibited him from bequeathing all his wealth and half, and only permitted bequeathing one-third, and said, 'One-third is also a lot.' Then when the owner (the deathly ill person) reached this stage, he became dispensed from the wealth, and his dispensation from wealth necessitates that the right of his heirs becomes attached to the wealth. Therefore, the right of the heirs became attached to the wealth, and a cause was established that the wealth would be transferred to the heirs. The attachment of the heirs' right to this wealth necessitates that even within one-third his disposition should not be effective. But due to a strong reason, permission for disposition through bequest was given with respect to this side, so that the shortcoming occurring from the original owner could be compensated. Hence, we did not manifest the testator's dispensation with respect to non-heirs to the extent of one-third. However, if he bequeaths to one of the heirs, then this dispensation will be manifested and his disposition will not be effective. Otherwise, it would cause harm to some heirs, because if the testator bequeaths to some heirs and not others, he gives preference to some over others, which causes harm and difficulty to some. In such a case, preference would necessarily occur, so it was declared impermissible altogether. And the hadith states that transgression is among the major sins, meaning a great sin. And transgression is interpreted as bequeathing more than one-third or bequeathing to an heir.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the limit of bequests in Hanafi law. The text begins by stating that a bequest for more than one-third of the estate is not valid. The proof is the well-known hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, where the Prophet ﷺ limited his will to one-third, saying 'one-third is a lot.' This establishes that beyond one-third is impermissible. The rationale is that upon death, the wealth becomes the right of the heirs. The testator's detachment from the wealth (due to approaching death) creates a cause for the transfer of ownership to the heirs. However, Islamic law permits the testator to exercise his right of bequest up to one-third for non-heirs, as a concession to compensate for any shortcomings in fulfilling good deeds. For heirs, bequests are not allowed because it would cause unfair preference among them, leading to discord. The hadith on 'transgression in the will' confirms that exceeding one-third or bequeathing to an heir is a major sin. This passage emphasizes the principle that the testator's freedom is limited to one-third, balancing his desire for charitable acts with the rights of legal heirs.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest or will made by a person regarding disposal of his property after death.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum amount that can be bequeathed to non-heirs without heirs' permission.
حیف (hayf): Transgression or injustice in a will, interpreted as exceeding one-third or bequeathing to an heir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One-quarter
B) One-third
C) One-half
D) The entire estate

Key Takeaway
Bequests exceeding one-third or to an heir are prohibited; the heirs' right to the estate overrides the testator's freedom beyond one-third.

Heirs' Permission for Bequests Exceeding One-Third
States the exception to the one-third limit for bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequests exceeding one-third and identify the conditions under which heirs' permission validates such a bequest.

Core Idea
A bequest exceeding one-third is invalid unless adult heirs permit after death, since they drop their right.

The general rule in Hanafi fiqh is that a bequest cannot exceed one-third of the estate without the consent of the heirs. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the exception: if the heirs, being adults, voluntarily allow the excess after the testator's death, the bequest becomes valid. This ruling is grounded in the principle that the prohibition exists to protect the heirs' right, and they are free to waive it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is bequeathing more than one-third of the estate. The default ruling is that it is not permissible (makruh tahriman or haram) because it infringes on heirs' rights.
Hanafi school considers it prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) if done without permission.
2
Locate the exception and its conditions
The exception is when the heirs give permission (ijazah) after the testator's death. The condition: heirs must be adults (baligh). Permission before death is not effective.
Why after death? Because the heirs' right only vests at the moment of death.
3
Understand the talil (reasoning)
The prohibition is solely to protect the heirs' right. Once they willingly drop that right after it vests, the legal impediment is removed.
This is a case of 'sitting of the right' (isqat al-haqq).
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Imagine a testator bequeaths half his estate to a non-heir. After death, all adult heirs agree. The bequest becomes valid for the full half. If any heir is a minor, the permission is not considered.
If some heirs are minors, the excess only applies to the shares of consenting adults? More details in other texts.
5
Compare with cross-madhhab view
The Shafi'i school allows permission during the testator's lifetime. The Hanafi restriction to after death is based on the nature of the heirs' right not being established until death.
This difference results in practical consequences: in Hanafi, a pre-death consent is irrelevant; in Shafi'i, it can validate the bequest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک تہائی سے زیادہ وصیت ورثہ کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے
قال الا ان يجيزها الورثة بعد موته وهم كبار لان الامتناع لحقهم وهم اسقطوه ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا مگر یہ کہ دورثہ اس کی ( ثلث سے زیادہ کی اجازت دے دیں موصی کے مرنے کے بعد حالانکہ وہ بڑے ہوں اس لئے کہ امتناع ان کے حق کی وجہ سے ہے اور انہوں نے اپنے حق کو ساقط کر دیا ہے۔
تشریح یعنی ایک تہائی سے زیادہ مال کی وصیت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے لیکن اگر مریض نے ایک تہائی سے زیادہ کی وصیت کر دی اور اس کے مرنے کے بعد ورثہ نے اس کی اجازت دیدی اور ورثہ بالغ ہوں تو پھر جائز ہے اس لئے کہ اس وصیت کا ممتنع ہونا ورثہ کے حق کی وجہ سے تھا اور جب انہوں نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔
The bequest exceeding one-third is dependent on the permission of the heirs. He said: Except if the heirs permit it after his death, while they are adults, because the prohibition is due to their right, and they have dropped it. Translation: Al-Quduri said: Except if the heirs give permission for it (bequest exceeding one-third) after the testator's death, while they are adults, because the prohibition is due to their right, and they have dropped it. Explanation: i.e., bequeathing more than one-third of the wealth is not permissible. But if the ill person made a bequest exceeding one-third, and after his death the heirs gave permission, and the heirs are adults, then it becomes permissible, because the prohibition was due to the right of the heirs, and when they dropped their right, it becomes permissible.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is a ruling that establishes an exception to the one-third limit. The basic prohibition on bequests exceeding one-third is not absolute; it is for the protection of the heirs' rights. Therefore, if the heirs, after the testator's death, voluntarily agree to allow the excess, the bequest becomes valid. The key condition is that the heirs must be adults (baligh) and give permission after the death, as their right only crystallizes at the moment of death. This illustrates a fundamental Hanafi principle: the right of the heirs is not established until death, so their consent during the testator's lifetime is not considered.

Key Terms
اجازت (ijazah): Permission given by the heirs after the testator's death to validate a bequest exceeding one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) After the testator's death
C) Either before or after
D) Only if the heirs are minors

Key Takeaway
A bequest exceeding one-third is void unless adult heirs voluntarily permit it after the testator's death, as they drop their right.

Timing of Heirs' Permission in Wasiyyah: During Life vs After Death
Explains why heirs' permission before death is revocable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle that heirs' permission given before the testator's death is revocable, and distinguish it from the binding nature of permission given after death.

Core Idea
A right not yet established cannot be waived permanently.

In Hanafi inheritance law, a bequest exceeding one-third of the estate requires the consent of the heirs. But when does that consent become final? This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies that the key factor is the timing of the heirs' right. Understanding this turns on a single concept: thubut al-haqq (establishment of the right).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is the heirs' permission for a bequest exceeding one-third. The ruling is that permission given during the testator's life is not binding, while permission after death is binding.
The ruling is about the bindingness of the permission, not the act of giving permission itself.
2
Identify the causal factor: thubut al-haqq
The heirs' right to the estate is established only at the moment of the testator's death. This temporal point determines the legal effect of any permission they give.
Thubut al-haqq is the key concept.
3
Distinguish the two scenarios
Before death: permission is given before the right exists, so it is not legally binding – the heirs may revoke after death. After death: permission is given after the right exists, so it is binding and cannot be retracted.
The analogy is that a right that has been dropped (by consent) ceases to exist.
4
Apply the principle to a hypothetical
Consider heirs who consent during the testator's final illness. Under Hanafi law, they may later revoke after death because their consent was before the right was established.
This protects heirs from being bound by hasty decisions during the testator's life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورثہ کی اجازت کا کب اعتبار ہوگا ؟
ولا معتبر با جازتهم في حال حياته لانها قبل ثبوت الحق اذا لحق يثبت عند الموت فكان لهم ان يردوه بعد وفاته بخلاف ما بعد الموت لانه بعد ثبوت الحق فليس لهم ان يرجعوا عنه لان الساقط متلاش ترجمہ اور موصی کی زندگی میں ورثہ کی اجازت کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ یہ (اس کی زندگی میں اجازت ) ثبوت حق سے پہلے ہے اس لئے کہ ورثہ کا حق موت کے وقت ثابت ہوتا ہے اور ورثہ کو حق ہو گا کہ وہ موصی کی وفات کے بعد اس اجازت کو ر دکر دیں بخلاف ما بعد الموت کے اس لئے کہ یہ اجازت ثبوت حق کے بعد ہے تو ورثہ کو اس سے رجوع کرنے کا حق نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ ساقط معدوم ہے۔
تشریح . اگر ورثہ نے مقدار ثلث سے زیادہ وصیت کی اجازت دے دی تو جائز ہے مگر اس میں یہ تفصیل ہے کہ اگر ورثہ کی
When will the permission of the heirs be considered? And no consideration is given to their permission during his (the testator's) life, because it is before the establishment of the right, for the right is established at death. Thus they have the right to reject it after his death, unlike after death, because it is after the establishment of the right, so they do not have the right to retract from it, because that which has been dropped is non-existent. Translation: And the permission of the heirs during the testator's life will not be considered, because this (permission during life) is before the establishment of the right, for the heirs' right is established at the time of death, and the heirs have the right to revoke that permission after the testator's death. Unlike after death, because this permission is after the establishment of the right, so the heirs do not have the right to retract from it, because that which has been dropped is nonexistent. Explanation: If the heirs give permission for a bequest exceeding one-third, it is permissible, but there is a detail: if the heirs... (incomplete)
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between permission given during the testator's life and after death. The key legal principle is that the heirs' right to the estate only becomes established at the moment of death. Therefore, any permission they give before death is not legally binding because it is issued before their right exists. They can revoke it after death. However, once they give permission after the testator's death, when their right is already established, that permission is final and cannot be retracted. The analogy is that a right that has been dropped (by consent) ceases to exist. This ruling protects the heirs from being bound by hasty decisions during the testator's illness.

Key Terms
ثبوت حق (thubut al-haqq): The establishment of the heirs' right to the estate, which occurs at the moment of the testator's death.
ساقط متلاش (saaqit mutalaashin): That which has been dropped is non-existent; an analogy for the irreversibility of a waiver after the right exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is permission given by heirs during the testator's life not considered binding?
A) Because they might change their mind
B) Because their right is not yet established
C) Because the testator can change his will
D) Because it is not in writing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the bindingness of heirs' permission in wasiyyah depends entirely on when the heirs' right is established — at death, not before.

The Prohibition of Bequest to an Heir and Definition of Hayf
Ruling on bequest to an heir with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequest to an heir and explain why it constitutes hayf (a major sin).

Core Idea
Bequest to an heir is invalid because it causes injury to other heirs.

This passage from the Hidayah establishes that a bequest to an heir is not only invalid but also a major sin. The text contrasts the permissibility of bequeathing to non-heirs within one-third with the absolute prohibition of bequeathing to an heir. The key term 'hayf' is defined as bequeathing more than one-third or to an heir, and it is supported by a hadith that declares it among the major sins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what the hukm (legal classification) is. The act is bequest (wasiyyah) to an heir. The ruling is that it is invalid (batil) and haram.
The passage explicitly states that such a disposition will not be effective.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Find the proof cited for the ruling. The text mentions a hadith that 'hayf is among the major sins.' The chain is not given, so it is a hadith ahad.
The dalil is a hadith, which is zanni al-thubut but still authoritative.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
Explain how the hadith proves the ruling. The hadith declares hayf a major sin. Hayf is then defined as bequeathing more than one-third or bequeathing to an heir. Therefore, bequeathing to an heir is a major sin, which implies prohibition and invalidity.
The definition of hayf is essential to connect the hadith to the specific act.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
Identify which school(s) disagree. The Shafi'i school permits bequest to an heir if the other heirs consent after death. This contrasts with the Hanafi position of absolute invalidity.
This difference has practical consequences (thamarah al-khilaf).
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
Determine which view is relied upon in the Hanafi school. The text presents the Hanafi position as the correct one, relying on the hadith and the principle of preventing harm to heirs. The mufta bihi is that the bequest is invalid and haram.
The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

ورثہ کے حق کا اس مال کے ساتھ تعلق اس بات کو مقتضی ہے کہ تہائی کے اندر بھی اس کا تصرف نافذ نہ ہوگر ای دلیل بزرکور کی وجہ سے اس . جانب کے حق میں تصرف وصیت کی اجازت دے دی گئی تا کہ اصل مالک کی جانب سے متحقق ہونے والی تقصیر دیت کا تدارک ہو سکے۔ لہذا ہم نے موصی کے استغناء کو مقدار ثلث میں اجانب کے حق میں ظاہر نہیں کیا۔

اور حیف کی تفسیر یہ ہے کہ تہائی سے زیادہ کی وصیت کرے یا وارث کے لئے وصیت کرے۔
The connection of the heirs' right to this property requires that even within one-third his disposition should not be effective. But due to a strong reason, permission was given for a bequest in favor of outsiders, so that the deficiency that occurred from the original owner can be remedied. Therefore, we did not manifest the testator's lack of need within one-third for outsiders. However, if he makes a bequest for one of the heirs, then this lack of need will manifest and his disposition will not be effective. Otherwise, injury to some heirs would become necessary because when the testator bequeaths to some heirs and not to others, he gives preference to some over others, which causes injury and hardship to some. In that case, the consequence is that preference becomes necessary, so it is declared invalid from the start. And it is stated in the hadith that hayf is among the major sins, i.e., a very great sin. And the explanation of hayf is to bequeath more than one-third or to bequeath for an heir.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling that a bequest to an heir is invalid. The text first explains that the testator's right to dispose of his estate within one-third is not invalidated for outsiders because a bequest to outsiders is permitted. However, if the testator makes a bequest to an heir, it is invalid because it would cause harm to other heirs by giving preference to some over others. This is supported by a hadith that considers such an act (hayf) to be among the major sins. The commentator defines hayf as either bequeathing more than one-third of the estate or bequeathing to an heir. This lesson establishes the principle that a bequest to an heir is not permissible under any circumstances because it leads to injustice among the heirs.

Key Terms
حیف (hayf): In this context, hayf means injustice in bequest, specifically bequeathing more than one-third of the estate or bequeathing to an heir, which is considered a major sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Bequeathing to an heir or bequeathing more than one-third
C) Bequeathing to a non-heir more than one-third
D) Bequeathing without witnesses

Key Takeaway
Bequest to an heir is absolutely invalid and constitutes hayf, a major sin, because it causes injustice to the other heirs.
