Bequest Beyond One-Third: Consent After Death Required
Stating the ruling that bequest beyond one-third requires heirs' consent after death, and that consent during life is invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for validating a bequest exceeding one-third and distinguish between consent given before and after death.

Core Idea
A bequest beyond one-third is valid only when heirs consent after death; consent during life is revocable.

This passage addresses a critical rule in Hanafi inheritance law: a bequest that exceeds one-third of the estate is initially invalid, but it can be validated if the heirs give their consent after the testator's death. The timing of consent is crucial, as consent given during the testator's lifetime is not binding. Understanding this distinction protects the rights of heirs and ensures the testator's wishes are honored within the limits of Shariah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a bequest exceeding one-third of the estate. The initial ruling is that it is invalid (batil) unless a condition is met.
2
Locate the condition for validity
The condition is the heirs' permission (ijazah) after the testator's death, provided the heirs are adults. This permission makes the bequest valid.
Consent after death is the key condition.
3
Analyze the timing distinction
Consent given during the testator's lifetime is not considered valid; heirs may revoke it after death. Consent after death is final and irrevocable.
4
Understand the rationale
The prohibition exists solely to protect the heirs' right, which vests only at death. Therefore, consent before vesting is not binding; consent after vesting drops the right permanently.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک تہائی سے زیادہ وصیت ورثہ کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے
قال الا ان يجيزها الورثة بعد موته وهم كبار لان الامتناع لحقهم وهم اسقطوه ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا مگر یہ کہ دورثہ اس کی ( ثلث سے زیادہ کی اجازت دے دیں موصی کے مرنے کے بعد حالانکہ وہ بڑے ہوں اس لئے کہ امتناع ان کے حق کی وجہ سے ہے اور انہوں نے اپنے حق کو ساقط کر دیا ہے۔
تشریح یعنی ایک تہائی سے زیادہ مال کی وصیت کرنا جائز نہیں ہے لیکن اگر مریض نے ایک تہائی سے زیادہ کی وصیت کر دی اور اس کے مرنے کے بعد ورثہ نے اس کی اجازت دیدی اور ورثہ بالغ ہوں تو پھر جائز ہے اس لئے کہ اس وصیت کا ممتنع ہونا ورثہ کے حق کی وجہ سے تھا اور جب انہوں نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔

ساقط معدوم ہے۔
تشریح . اگر ورثہ نے مقدار ثلث سے زیادہ وصیت کی اجازت دے دی تو جائز ہے مگر اس میں یہ تفصیل ہے کہ اگر ورثہ کی اجازت موسی کی موت کے بعد ہے تو اجازت درست ہے اور اب ورثہ کو اپنی اجازت سے پھرنے کا حق نہیں ہے اور اگر ورثہ کی اجازت موصی کی زندگی میں ہو تو ابھی اس اجازت کا کوئی اعتبار نہ ہوگا بلکہ ورثہ کو بعد موت موصی اس اجازت سے پھرنے کا اختیار ہوگا کیونکہ موت موصی سے پہلے ورثہ کا حق ثابت ہی نہیں ہوا تو اجازت بھی ان کی معتبر نہ ہوگی لیکن موت کے بعد ان کا حق ثابت ہو گیا تو جب انہوں نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا یعنی اجازت دے دی تو اب حق ساقط ہو گیا اور جو ساقط ہو گیا وہ نہ ہونے کے درجہ میں ہو گیا۔
Bequest beyond one-third is dependent on the permission of the heirs. He (Quduri) said: Except if the heirs give permission for it after his death while they are adults, because the prohibition is due to their right, and they have dropped it. Translation: Quduri said: Except if the heirs give permission for it (more than one-third) after the death of the testator, while they are adults, because the prohibition is due to their right, and they have dropped their right. Explanation: That is, bequeathing more than one-third of the property is not permissible. But if the sick person made a bequest of more than one-third and after his death the heirs gave permission for it and the heirs are adults, then it is permissible, because the prohibition of this bequest was due to the right of the heirs, and when they dropped their right, it becomes permissible. When will the heirs' permission be considered? And their permission during his lifetime is not considered, because it is before the establishment of the right, so the right is established at death, so they have the right to reject it after his death, unlike after death, because it is after the establishment of the right, so they do not have the right to revoke it, because that which has dropped is non-existent. Explanation: If the heirs gave permission for a bequest of more than one-third, it is permissible. But there is a detail: if the heirs' permission is after the death of the testator, then the permission is valid, and now the heirs do not have the right to withdraw from their permission. And if the heirs' permission is during the lifetime of the testator, then this permission has no validity, rather the heirs have the option to withdraw from this permission after the death of the testator, because before the testator's death the heirs' right was not established, so their permission is not valid. But after death, their right is established, so when they dropped their right i.e., gave permission, then the right has fallen away, and that which has fallen away is like non-existent.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage establishes a key ruling in Hanafi inheritance law: a bequest exceeding one-third of the estate is initially invalid, but it becomes valid if the heirs give their consent after the testator's death, provided they are adults. The reason is that the prohibition exists solely to protect the heirs' rights. When they willingly waive their right, the bequest is enforced. The passage then addresses the timing of consent. Consent given during the testator's lifetime is not binding because the heirs' right does not fully vest until death. Therefore, they may revoke it after death. However, consent given after death is final and irrevocable because the right has vested and has been dropped. This lesson teaches the student the conditions for validating a bequest beyond one-third and the critical distinction between pre-death and post-death consent.

Key Terms
إجازة الورثة (ijazat al-wuratha): Permission given by the heirs for a bequest exceeding one-third or for a bequest to an heir, which after death makes the bequest valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When given after the testator's death
C) When given before the testator falls ill
D) When given at any time before the distribution of the estate

Key Takeaway
A bequest beyond one-third requires the heirs' consent after death; pre-death consent is voidable.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

The Invalidity of Pre-Death Consent and the Concept of Isnad
Answer to an implicit objection about retroactive attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pre-death consent in bequests and explain why the concept of isnad (retroactive attribution) does not validate it.

Core Idea
Pre-death consent is invalid because the permission perishes and ownership vests only at death.

In Hanafi law, a bequest (wasiyyah) exceeding one-third of the estate requires the consent of the heirs. But what if the heirs consent during the testator's terminal illness and later revoke? This passage clarifies that such pre-death consent is legally ineffective, even if the heirs had a contingent right to the estate. The key is the concept of isnad (retroactive attribution) and the distinction between a mere right and full ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the implicit objection
Read the passage to understand the core Hanafi ruling: heirs' consent given before death is invalid. Then note the implicit objection: since the heirs' right attaches from the illness, their consent should be valid by retroactive attribution (isnad), similar to guarantee cases.
The objection is a typical student misconception.
2
Analyze the answer: two reasons
The passage gives two reasons: (1) The heirs lack authority to dispose of the property during the testator's life. (2) Retroactive attribution requires the thing (consent) to exist at the time of attribution, but the consent has perished. Additionally, full ownership (haqiqah) vests only at death, so isnad would improperly convert a right into ownership before death.
Focus on the second reason as the proof.
3
Examine the dalil (proof)
The dalil is a rational proof: 'And because real ownership is established at death, and before it mere right is established. So if isnad were applied, the right would turn into reality before death.' This is a logical argument (dalil aqli) distinguishing between haqq and haqiqah.
The text explicitly quotes the Arabic proof.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Imagine a testator bequeaths 1/3 to a non-heir. Heirs say 'we allow it' during his illness. After death, they revoke. According to this ruling, their pre-death consent is void, and they can reject the bequest. Only consent given after death is binding.
This also illustrates why pre-death consent is not binding.
5
Compare with other areas of fiqh where isnad is accepted
The objection mentions usurpation (ghasb) where isnad is accepted. The Hanafi response shows that in ghasb, the right being retroactively attributed (the guarantee) still exists, whereas here the consent itself no longer exists. This nuanced distinction is critical.
This comparison deepens understanding of isnad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غایة البیان میں لان الساقط متلاش کا تعلق موصی کی حیات میں اجازت دینے سے کیا ہے یعنی اس وقت میں ورنہ کی اجازت ساقط ہے اور ساقط معدوم کے درجہ میں ہے اور جب وہ معدوم کے درجہ میں ہے تو اس اجازت کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے لہذ اور شہ کو اس کی تردید کا حق ہے۔
سوال مقدر کا جواب
غاية الامرانه يستند عند الاجازة لكن الاستناد يظهر فى حق القائم وهذا قد مضى وتلاشى ترجمہ غایہ الامر یہ ہے کہ حق کا استناد بوقت اجازت ہوگا لیکن استناد تو امر موجود میں ظاہر ہوتا ہے حالانکہ یہ ( قبل الموت کی اجازت ) گزرگئی اور معدوم ہو گئی ہے۔
تشریح یہ حقیقت میں ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے۔
سوال موت سے پہلے ورثہ نے جو اجازت دی تھی وہ بھی اپنے حق میں دی تھی ، کیونکہ میت کے مال میں ورثہ کا جو حق ہے وہ مرض موت کے وقت سے ہے تو جب بطریق استناد بوقت اجازت ورثہ ان کا حق ثابت ہو گیا تو ان کی اجازت معتبر ہونی چاہئے جیسے
غصب میں؟
جواب اگر چہ وارثوں کا حق میت کے ابتدائی مرض ہی سے اس مال کے ساتھ متعلق ہو جاتا ہے لیکن ایک تو ان کو تصرف کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ دوسرے یہ کہ استناد کے لئے اس چیز کی بقاء کی ضرورت ہے جس کو بطریق استناد ثابت کرنے کی کوشش کی جارہی ہے اور وہ اجازت ہے حالانکہ جو اجازت قبل الموت دی گئی تھی اب وہ معدوم ہو چکی ہے لہذا بطریق استناد بھی اس اجازت کا
ثبوت نہ ہو سکے گا۔
مذکورہ جواب کی مزید وضاحت
ولان الحقيقة تثبت عند الموت وقبله يثبت مجرد الحق فلو استند من كل وجه ينقلب حقيقة قبله والرضا ببطلان الحق لا يكون رضا ببطلان الحقيقة
ترجمہ اور اس لئے کہ ملک حقیقی موت کے وقت ثابت ہوتی ہے اور موت سے پہلے محض حق ثابت ہوتا ہے پس اگر ہر ہر اعتبار سے استناد ثابت ہو جائے تو حق حقیقت سے بدل جائے گا موت سے پہلے ہی اور بطلان حق سے راضی ہونا بطلان حقیقت سے راضی ہونا
In Ghayat al-Bayan, the phrase 'because the dropped is non-existent' is related to giving permission during the testator's lifetime, meaning that at that time the heirs' permission is dropped and the dropped is of the status of non-existent, and when it is of the status of non-existent, then that permission has no validity. Therefore, the heirs have the right to reject it. Answer to an implicit question: The utmost is that it is retroactively attributed at the time of permission, but retroactive attribution manifests for a right that exists, and this (permission before death) has passed and become non-existent. Explanation: This is actually an answer to an implicit question. Question: The permission that the heirs gave before death was also given regarding their right, because the heirs' right to the deceased's property exists from the time of the death illness. So when by way of retroactive attribution at the time of permission the heirs' right becomes established, then their permission should be valid, like in the case of usurpation? Answer: Although the heirs' right becomes attached to this property from the initial illness, firstly, they do not have the authority of disposition. Secondly, for retroactive attribution, the existence of the thing that is being sought to be established by retroactive attribution is required, and that is the permission, while the permission given before death has now become non-existent. Therefore, by way of retroactive attribution too, this permission cannot be established. Further clarification of the mentioned answer: And because real ownership is established at death, and before it mere right is established. So if retroactive attribution were established from every aspect, the right would turn into reality before death, and being satisfied with the nullification of the right is not being satisfied with the nullification of the reality.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage addresses an implicit objection: Since the heirs' right is attached to the estate from the beginning of the death illness, why isn't their consent given during the testator's lifetime valid through the concept of isnad (retroactive attribution), similar to how a guarantee (daman) can be retroactively validated? The answer is twofold. First, the heirs lack the authority to dispose of the property during the testator's lifetime. Second, retroactive attribution requires the thing being attributed (the consent) to still exist at the time of attribution, but the pre-death consent has perished and is non-existent. Furthermore, ownership (al-haqiqa) vests only at death; before death there is merely a right (haqq). If retroactive attribution were applied, it would convert the right into full ownership before death, which would alter the nature of the right. Therefore, the rule stands: only post-death consent is valid and binding.

Key Terms
استناد (istinād): Retroactive attribution; the concept that a legal effect can be attributed back to a previous time under certain conditions, e.g., in cases of guarantee or purchase.
حقيقة (haqiqah): In this context, actual ownership of the property, which vests at death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the heirs' consent given during the testator's lifetime not valid through the concept of isnad (retroactive attribution)?
A) Because the hadith prohibits it
B) Because the consent perishes and cannot be retroactively attributed, and because full ownership vests only at death
C) Because the heirs are not adults
D) Because the testator can revoke the bequest

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that heirs' consent given before the testator's death is invalid because the consent perishes and cannot be retroactively attributed, and because full ownership vests only at death.

Killer's Bequest and Heirs' Approval: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of bequest to killer after heirs' permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the validity of a bequest to a killer and apply the relied-upon ruling when heirs give permission.

Core Idea
A killer's bequest becomes valid with heirs' permission because the disqualification protects their rights, not as a punishment.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute about a bequest made to a person who killed the testator. The central question is whether the other heirs can waive the killer's disqualification by giving their permission after the testator's death. The two elders (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say yes, while Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the disqualification is a punishment that cannot be waived. We will analyze the proofs on both sides and conclude with the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine the specific scenario: a testator makes a bequest to his killer, and the other heirs give permission after death. What is the ruling?
2
State the two positions
The two elders (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that the bequest becomes valid with permission. Abu Yusuf holds it remains invalid.
3
Analyze the proofs
For the two elders: the prohibition is for the heirs' benefit, so they can waive it. For Abu Yusuf: the disqualification is a punishment ('uquba) that cannot be waived.
The two elders refute Abu Yusuf by noting that accidental killers are also deprived, yet they are not subject to punishment.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position is that of the two elders because the disqualification is not punitive: both intentional and accidental killers are treated equally.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: if heirs approve, the killer receives the bequest according to the two elders, but not according to Abu Yusuf.

تشریح ابھی ماقبل میں گزرا ہے کہ قاتل وصیت سے بھی محروم ہوتا ہے اور میراث سے بھی لیکن اگر موصی نے قاتل کے لئے وصیت کر دی اور ورثہ نے اس کی اجازت دیدی تو اب کیا حکم ہے؟ تو اس میں حضرات طرفین اور امام ابو یوسف کا اختلاف ہے امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر ورثہ اجازت دیدیں تب بھی وصیت جائز نہ ہوگی اور حضرات طرفین فرماتے ہیں کہ اب وصیت جائز ہوگی۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ورثہ کے اجازت دینے سے قاتل کا وہ جرم ختم نہ ہوگا جس کی وجہ سے وہ وصیت سے محروم کیا گیا تھا اور جب وہ جرم ختم نہیں ہوگا تو قاتل کا جرمان بھی بدستور برقرار رہے گا۔ حضرات طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قاتل کو میراث سے محروم کرنے کا اصل راز حق ورثہ ہے اس لئے کہ بطلان وصیت کا نفع ورثہ کو ہوتا ہے جیسے اگر قاتل کو میراث سے محروم کر دیا جائے تو اس کا نفع بھی ورثہ کو ہوتا ہے۔ اور ورثہ جیسے اپنے میں سے کسی ایک کے لئے وصیت سے راضی نہیں ہوتے اس طرح وہ قاتل کے لئے بھی وصیت سے راضی نہ ہوں گے لیکن اگر وہ اپنے میں سے کسی وارث کے لئے وصیت سے راضی ہو جائیں اور اس وصیت کی اجازت دیدیں تو وصیت جائز ہو جاتی ہے اسی طرح اگر ورثہ قاتل کے لئے بھی اجازت دیدیں تو وصیت جائز ہو جائے گی۔ اور امام ابو یوسف کا یہ فرمانا کہ قاتل کا وصیت سے محروم ہونا عقوبت کے طریقہ پر ہے یہ غیر مسلم ہے کیونکہ اس میں عامد اور خاطی دونوں برابر ہیں حالانکہ خاطی مستحق عقوبت نہیں ہوتا۔
Explanation: It has already passed earlier that a killer is deprived of both bequest and inheritance. But if the testator made a bequest for the killer and the heirs gave their permission, what is the ruling? In this, there is a difference between the two elders (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Imam Abu Yusuf. Imam Abu Yusuf says: Even if the heirs give permission, the bequest will not be valid. The two elders say: Now the bequest will be valid. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that the killer's crime, due to which he was deprived of the bequest, will not be eliminated by the heirs' permission, and when that crime is not eliminated, the killer's punishment remains in effect. The two elders' proof is that the real reason for depriving the killer of inheritance is the right of the heirs, because the benefit of invalidating the bequest goes to the heirs, just as if the killer is deprived of inheritance, its benefit also goes to the heirs. And just as the heirs are not satisfied with a bequest for one of themselves, similarly they will not be satisfied with a bequest for the killer. But if they become satisfied with a bequest for one of their heirs and give permission for that bequest, the bequest becomes valid. Similarly, if the heirs give permission for the killer, the bequest becomes valid. And Imam Abu Yusuf's statement that the killer's deprivation of bequest is by way of punishment is not accepted, because in this both intentional and accidental killers are equal, whereas an accidental killer is not deserving of punishment.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a bequest made to a person who killed the testator. The two elders (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that if the other heirs give their permission after the testator's death, the bequest becomes valid. Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the killer's disqualification is a punishment ('uquba) that cannot be removed by the heirs' permission. The text then refutes Abu Yusuf's position by pointing out that both intentional and accidental killers are treated equally, whereas accidental killers are not subject to punishment, indicating the disqualification is not punitive but based on the rights of the heirs.

Key Terms
قاتل (qātil): One who kills the testator, whether intentionally or accidentally, who is deprived of bequest and inheritance.
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest made by a testator, to be executed after death, limited to one-third of the estate.
ورثہ (warathah): The heirs of the deceased who are entitled to inherit.
اجازت (ijāzat): Permission given by the heirs after the testator's death to allow a bequest that was otherwise prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The bequest becomes valid.
B) The bequest remains invalid because the killer's crime is not expiated.
C) The bequest becomes valid only if the killer was accidental.
D) The bequest becomes valid only if the killer repents.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a bequest to a killer becomes valid if the other heirs give their permission.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Prohibition of Bequest to an Heir and the Time of Assessment
Ruling with proof, exceptions, and comparative analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequest to an heir and explain why the status of being an heir is assessed at death, using the hadith and legal reasoning.

Core Idea
A bequest to an heir is prohibited; heir status is fixed at death, not at the bequest time.

This lesson examines the fundamental rule that a bequest (wasiyyah) to an heir is not permissible, supported by the Prophet's ﷺ hadith. We will explore the reasoning behind this prohibition, and then clarify a crucial point: whether an individual is considered an heir at the time of the bequest or at the time of death. Additionally, we will compare bequest with two other transactions made during death illness: gift (hiba) and acknowledgment (iqrar), highlighting how each is assessed differently. Finally, we cover the scenario where heirs may permit a prohibited bequest after the testator's death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule and Its Evidence
The text states that a bequest to an heir is not permissible. The primary evidence is the hadith: 'Indeed Allah has given every rightful person his right. Indeed, no bequest to an heir.' Understand that this is a primary proof (dalil) from the Sunnah.
The hadith is ahad, but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala) regarding the prohibition.
2
Understand the Rationale for Prohibition
The prohibition is based on two reasons: (1) It harms other heirs by preferring some over others, leading to severance of family ties; (2) It is considered injustice (hayf) because Allah has already fixed inheritance shares.
The protection of heirs' rights is the underlying wisdom.
3
Determine When Heir Status is Evaluated
The text explicitly states that the status of being an heir is considered at the time of death, not at the time of the bequest. This is because a bequest is a transfer of ownership that takes effect after death. Example: if a bequest is made to a brother who later ceases to be an heir (e.g., a son is born), the bequest becomes valid.
This is a key Hanafi principle: the moment of vesting is death.
4
Distinguish Bequest from Gift and Acknowledgment in Death Illness
In death illness (marad al-mawt), a gift (hiba) to an heir is treated like a bequest: it is assessed at death and executed from one-third. An acknowledgment (iqrar) to an heir, however, is a present transaction, so the heir status is considered at the time of acknowledgment, not at death.
This distinction arises because iqrar is a present binding declaration, not contingent on death.
5
Apply the Exception: Heirs' Permission and Partial Approval
If all heirs give permission after the testator's death, a bequest to an heir becomes valid. If only some permit, the bequest is valid to the extent of the permitting heir's share and void for the others.
The prohibition exists for the right of the heirs, so they may waive it.

He (al-Quduri) said: And it is not permissible for (the testator's) heir, because of his ﷺ saying: 'Indeed Allah the Exalted has given every rightful person his right. Indeed, no bequest to an heir.' And because some are harmed by preferring others, so permitting it would sever family ties. And because it is injustice by the hadith we narrated. And consideration of whether one is an heir or not is at the time of death, not at the time of the bequest, because it is a transfer of ownership attached to after death, and its ruling is established after death. And the gift (hiba) from a sick person to an heir is in this respect analogous to a bequest, because it is a bequest in ruling, so it is executed from the one-third. And the acknowledgment (iqrar) of a sick person to an heir is opposite to it, because it is a transaction in the present, so consideration is at the time of acknowledgment. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And a bequest to the testator's heir is not permissible, because of the Prophet's ﷺ saying: 'Allah has given every rightful person his right. Be aware, no bequest to an heir.' And because some will be harmed due to preferring others, so permitting it would sever family ties. And because making a bequest to an heir is injustice, due to the hadith we narrated. And consideration of whether one is an heir or not is at the time of death, not at the time of the bequest, because a bequest is a transfer of ownership attached to after death, and its ruling is established after death. And the gift from a sick person to an heir is in this regard similar to a bequest (in that consideration of being heir is at death), because a gift is a bequest in ruling, so that it is executed from the one-third. And the acknowledgment of a sick person to an heir is opposite to it, because it is a transaction in the present, so it will be considered at the time of acknowledgment. Explanation: Just as a bequest for a killer is not permissible, similarly a bequest for an heir is not permissible. First, because the hadith prohibits bequest to an heir, since Allah has given every rightful person his right through inheritance, so what meaning would a bequest to an heir have? Second, because doing so involves preferring some heirs over others, which becomes a means of severing ties of kinship. Also, making a bequest to an heir is called injustice in the hadith. Then consideration of whether one is an heir or not is not at the time of bequest but at the time of death. Hence, if a sick person made a bequest for his brother, and after the bequest a son was born to the sick person, then the brother is no longer an heir, so the bequest is valid, even though at the time of bequest he was an heir. And consideration of the time of death is made because the meaning of bequest is a transfer of ownership attached to after death, so consideration of being an heir is also at that time, and the ruling of the bequest is established after death. Therefore, consideration of being an heir or not is at the time of death, not at the time of bequest. If a sick person gives a gift during death illness, his gift is also in the category of bequest, so it will not be valid for an heir, and here also consideration of being an heir is at the time of death, not at the time of gift, because legally the gift is in the category of bequest. This is why, just as a bequest is executed from the one-third, similarly this is also executed from the one-third. And if a sick person makes an acknowledgment (iqrar) to an heir, this acknowledgment is not valid, but here consideration of being an heir is at the time of acknowledgment, not at the time of death. Therefore, here the time of acknowledgment is considered. If some heirs give permission for a bequest to the killer or heir and some do not, what is the ruling? He (al-Quduri) said: Unless the heirs permit it. And this exception is narrated in the hadith we narrated, and because the prohibition is for their right, so it becomes permissible by their permission. And if some permit and some reject, it is valid for the one who permitted to the extent of his share, due to his authority over himself, and it is void regarding the one who rejected. Translation: Al-Quduri said: Unless the heirs make it permissible. And this exception is narrated in the hadith we narrated, and because the prohibition is for their right, so the bequest is permissible by their permission. And if some permit and some reject, it is valid for the one who permitted to the extent of his share, due to his authority over himself, and it is void regarding the one who rejected. Explanation: A bequest for an heir is not permissible, but if the heirs give permission, then it is permissible, because the prohibition was only for their right.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage establishes the rule that a bequest to an heir is prohibited, supported by the hadith 'No bequest to an heir' (la wasiyya li-warith). The reasoning is that Allah has already assigned shares to heirs through inheritance, so a bequest would upset the distribution, cause resentment, and sever family ties. The text then clarifies a crucial point: the status of being an heir is determined at the time of death, not at the time the bequest is made. For example, if a person bequeaths to his brother and later has a son, the brother ceases to be an heir, so the bequest becomes valid. This is because a bequest is a transfer of ownership that takes effect after death. The passage also compares three transactions from a sick person: (1) a bequest to an heir is assessed at death, (2) a gift (hiba) to an heir is treated like a bequest and also assessed at death, and (3) an acknowledgment (iqrar) to an heir is assessed at the time of acknowledgment because it is a present transaction. Finally, the text addresses partial approval by heirs: if some heirs permit a bequest that was prohibited (e.g., to an heir) and others reject it, the bequest is valid for the permitting heirs to the extent of their shares, but void for the rejecting ones. The commentary reiterates that the prohibition exists for the protection of the heirs' rights, so they may waive it.

Key Terms
وارث (wārith): A person entitled to inherit from the deceased at the time of death.
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest that takes effect after death, transferring ownership of up to one-third of the estate.
ہبہ (hibah): A gift, which when made by a person in death illness (marad al-mawt) is treated like a bequest in terms of execution from one-third and consideration of heir status at death.
اقرار (iqrar): An acknowledgment of debt or ownership, which is a present transaction and thus valid even if made to an heir, but consideration of heir status is at the time of acknowledgment.
اجازت (ijazat): Permission given by heirs after the testator's death to validate a bequest that was otherwise prohibited (e.g., to an heir or to a killer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the status of being an heir determined for a bequest?
A) At the time the bequest is made.
B) At the time of the testator's death.
C) At the time of the heirs' approval.
D) At the time of the testator's illness.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to an heir is prohibited unless all heirs give permission after death; heir status is assessed at death, not at the time of the bequest.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Bequest to an Heir: Invalidity and Timing of Heirship
Ruling with proof: prohibition of bequest to heir, timing rule, and comparison with hiba and iqrar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a bequest to an heir is invalid, explain the proof from hadith, and apply the rule that heirship is determined at death to distinguish between wasiyyah, hiba in marad al-mawt, and iqrar.

Core Idea
No bequest to an heir – heirship is assessed at death, not at the time of the will.

In this lesson, we examine the prohibition of making a bequest to someone who is an heir. The Hanafi school relies on the prophetic hadith 'La wasiyyata li-warith' and a rationale of preventing discord among heirs. Crucially, the status of being an heir is judged at the moment of death, not when the will is written. This principle also applies to gifts made during terminal illness, but not to acknowledgments of debt, which are treated as immediate dispositions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
State that a bequest to an heir is invalid (haram) based on the hadith 'La wasiyyata li-warith' and the rationale that it gives preference among heirs.
The hadith is ahad, so the prohibition is zanni but firmly established.
2
Understand the timing of heirship
Heirship is evaluated at the time of death, not at the time of the will. This is because a bequest is a transfer attached to death.
Example: if a brother is an heir at the will's writing but later a son is born, the brother ceases to be an heir at death.
3
Apply to similar transactions
A gift (hiba) made during terminal illness is treated like a bequest: it must come from one-third and heirship is considered at death. An acknowledgment (iqrar) to an heir is invalid, but heirship is considered at the time of the acknowledgment because it is immediate.
This distinction hinges on whether the disposition is deferred (attached to death) or immediate.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school permits a bequest to an heir up to one-third without consent, while the Hanafi school requires the consent of all heirs after death for validity.
This difference arises from different interpretations of the hadith and the rationale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
یہاں تک کہ یہ تہائی سے نافذ ہوتا ہے اور وارث کے لئے مریض کا اقرار اس کے برعکس ہے اس لئے کہ یہ فی الحال تصرف ہے تو یہ اقرار کے وقت معتبر ہوگا۔
تشریح جس طرح قاتل کے لئے وصیت جائز نہیں اسی طرح وارث کیلئے بھی وصیت جائز نہیں ہے، اولا تو اس لئے کہ حدیث میں وارث کے لئے وصیت سے منع فرما دیا گیا ہے کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ہر حق والے کو اس کا حق خود دید یا یعنی میراث کے ذریعہ تو پھر وارث کے لئے وصیت کے کیا معنی ہوں گے۔

الہذا اگر کسی مریض نے اپنے بھائی کے لئے وصیت کی اور بعد وصیت مریض کے لڑکا پیدا ہو گیا تو اب بھائی وارث نہیں رہا لہذا وصیت جائز ہے اگر چہ بوقت وصیت یہ وارث تھا۔ اور وقت موت کا اعتبار اس لئے کیا گیا ہے کہ وصیت کے معنی ہی وہ تملیک ہے جو مابعد الموت کی جانب مضاف ہو تو وارث ہونے کا اعتبار بھی اس وقت کیا جائے گا اور وصیت کا حکم بھی موت کے بعد ثابت ہوتا ہے لہذا وارث ہونے یا نہ ہونے کا اعتبار بھی بوقت موت ہوگا نہ کہ بوقت وصیت۔
اگر مریض مرض الموت میں ہبہ کرے تو اس کا ہیہ بھی وصیت کے درجہ میں ہے لہذا وارث کے لئے یہ بھی معتبر نہ ہوگا اور یہاں بھی وارث ہونے کا اعتبار بوقت موت ہوگا نہ کہ بوقت وصیت کیونکہ حکما ہبہ وصیت کے درجہ میں ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ جس طرح وصیت تہائی کے اندر نافذ ہوتی ہے اسی طرح یہ بھی تہائی کے اندر نافذ ہوتا ہے۔ اور اگر مریض وارث کے لئے اقرار کرے تو یہ اقرار غیر معتبر ہے لیکن یہاں وارث ہونے کا اعتبار بوقت اقرار ہے نہ کہ بوقت موت لہذا یہاں وقت اقرار کا اعتبار ہوگا۔
Until it is executed from one-third, and the acknowledgment of a sick person for an heir is contrary to that, because it is a present disposition, so it will be valid at the time of acknowledgment. Explanation: Just as a bequest to a murderer is not permissible, similarly a bequest to an heir is not permissible. Firstly, because the hadith prohibits a bequest to an heir, since Allah has given every rightful person his right through inheritance. Secondly, because it gives preference to some heirs over others, which leads to severance of family ties. And the consideration of being an heir is not at the time of the will but at the time of death. So if a sick person makes a bequest to his brother, and then a son is born to the sick person, the brother is no longer an heir, so the bequest is valid. The consideration at death is because the bequest is a transfer attached to after death. If a sick person makes a gift (hiba) during his terminal illness, it is at the level of a bequest, so it is not valid for an heir, and also consideration is at death. But if he makes an acknowledgment (iqrar) for an heir, it is invalid, and here consideration is at the time of acknowledgment, not at death.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the prohibition of bequest to an heir, citing a hadith that forbids it. The reasoning is that inheritance shares are divinely ordained, and favoring one heir over another creates discord. Crucially, the heir status is assessed at the time of death, not when the will is written. For example, if a man wills to his brother (who is an heir at the time of will) but later has a son, the brother ceases to be an heir, and the will becomes valid. The same rule applies to gifts (hiba) made during terminal illness (marad al-mawt) because they are treated like bequests, operating within the one-third limit and considering heirship at death. However, an acknowledgment (iqrar) of a debt to an heir is treated differently: it is a present disposition, so the heir status is checked at the time of the acknowledgment. This distinction is based on the nature of the transaction—iqrar is immediate, while wasiyyah and hiba (from marad al-mawt) are deferred.

Key Terms
وصیت (wasiyyah): A bequest or will made by a person regarding his property to take effect after death.
وارث (warith): An heir entitled to a share of the deceased's estate through inheritance.
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A fatal illness that gives rise to fear of death and often leads to death.
اقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right or debt owed to another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man during his terminal illness makes a bequest to his brother. At the time of the will, the brother is his only heir. Later, the man has a son and then dies. What is the ruling?
A) The bequest is invalid because the brother was an heir at the time of the will.
B) The bequest is valid because at death the brother is no longer an heir due to the son.
C) The bequest is valid only up to one-third of the estate.
D) The bequest is invalid because the brother is still an heir.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to an heir is prohibited; heirship is determined at death, not at the time of the will, and this rule applies similarly to gifts made during terminal illness but not to acknowledgments.

Partial Consent of Heirs to a Bequest for an Heir
Ruling with proof on partial consent of heirs to a bequest for an heir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that when some heirs consent to a bequest for an heir, the bequest is valid from their shares and void from the shares of those who reject, citing the hadith and the principle of wilayah.

Core Idea
A bequest to an heir is invalid unless the heirs consent; partial consent gives partial effect.

This lesson examines the scenario where a testator makes a bequest to an heir, which is normally prohibited. However, the prohibition exists to protect the rights of the other heirs. When some heirs consent after death, they waive their right, making the bequest enforceable from their shares. The Hanafi school derives this from the hadith and the principle that each heir has authority over his own right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
State that a bequest to an heir is generally prohibited (haraam) without the consent of the other heirs. The default ruling is invalidity.
The prohibition is not absolute but contingent on the heirs' rights.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'لا تجوز الوصية لوارث إلا أن يشاء الورثة' (No bequest to an heir is valid unless the heirs wish). This is a sunnah ahad with zanni transmission and indication.
The exception phrase 'إلا أن يشاء الورثة' is key.
3
Understand the exception
The word 'إلا' indicates that the prohibition is removed if the heirs express their wish (consent). The prohibition is for the right of the heirs, not an absolute divine command.
Thus, permission turns the prohibited into permissible.
4
Analyze the scenario of partial consent
When some heirs consent and some reject, the bequest is valid only to the extent of the consenting heirs' shares. This is because each heir has wilayah (authority) over his own right and can waive it.
The rejecting heir retains his right; the bequest is void regarding his share.
5
Derive the ruling
The mufta bihi position: the bequest is valid pro-rata based on the shares of consenting heirs, and void for the shares of rejecting heirs.
This is established in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعض ورثا قاتل وارث کیلئے وصیت کی اجازت دیں اور بعض اجازت نہ دیں تو کیا حکم ہوگا ؟
قال الا ان يجزيها الورثة ويروى هذا الاستثناء فيما رويناه ولان الامتناع لحقهم فتجوز باجازتهم ولو اجاز بعض ورد بعض تجوز على المجيز بقدر حصته لولايته عليه وبطل في حق الراد.
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا مگر یہ کہ اس وصیت کو ورثا جائز قرار دیدیں اور یہ استثناء اس حدیث میں مروی ہے جس کو ہم نے روایت کیا ہے اور اس لئے کہ وصیت کا ممتنع ہونا ورثا کے حق کی وجہ سے ہے تو وصیت ان کی اجازت سے جائز ہے اور اگر بعض نے اجازت دی اور بعض نے رد کیا تو اجازت دینے والے پر اس کے حصہ کے بقدر جائز ہے اپنے اوپر مجیز کی ولایت کی وجہ سے اور رد کرنے والے کے حق میں وصیت باطل ہے۔
تشریح وارث کے لئے وصیت جائز نہیں ہے لیکن اگر ورنا اجازت دیدیں تو پھر جائز ہے اس لئے کہ امتناع انہی کے حق کی وجہ سے تھا
تو جب انھوں نے اجازت دیدی تو جائز ہو گئی ۔
اور یہ استثناء حدیث کے اندر بھی موجود ہے کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے، لا تجوز الوصية لوارث الا ان يشاء الورثة. اور اگر بعض ورثا نے اجازت دیدی اور بعض نے اجازت نہیں دی بلکہ اس کو رد کر دیا تو زد کرنے والے کے حق میں وصیت باطل ہو گئی اور اجازت دینے والے کے حق میں اپنے حصہ کے بقدر درست ہے کیونکہ نجیز کو اپنے اوپر ولایت ہے۔
If some heirs give permission for a bequest to an [...] heir and some do not, what is the ruling? He (Quduri) said: Except if the heirs ratify it. This exception is narrated in the hadith we have related, and because the prohibition is for their right, so it becomes permissible by their permission. And if some give permission and some reject, it is valid for the one who permitted to the extent of his share, due to his authority over himself, and it is invalid with respect to the one who rejected. Translation: They said: Except if the heirs make it valid. And this exception is narrated in the hadith that we have related. And because the prohibition of the bequest is due to the right of the heirs, so it is valid by their permission. And if some permitted and some rejected, it is valid for the one who permitted to the extent of his share, because he has authority over himself, and it is invalid with respect to the one who rejected. Explanation: A bequest to an heir is not permissible, but if the heirs permit it, then it becomes permissible, because the prohibition was for their right. So when they permitted, it became valid. And this exception is also present in the hadith: 'No bequest to an heir except if the heirs wish.' And if some heirs permitted and some did not, but rather rejected, then in the right of the rejecter the bequest becomes invalid, and in the right of the one who permitted it is valid to the extent of his share, because the one who permitted has authority over himself.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof dealing with the scenario where some heirs consent to a bequest that would otherwise be invalid because the beneficiary is an heir. The original prohibition is based on the hadith 'La wasiyyata li-warith' (No bequest to an heir). However, the prohibition is for the right of the other heirs, not an absolute divine command. Therefore, if all heirs consent after the testator's death, the bequest becomes valid. If only some consent, the bequest is enforceable only from their respective shares of the estate. For example, if two heirs have equal shares and one consents while the other rejects, the bequest is partly valid (from the consenting heir's share) and partly void (from the rejecting heir's share). This is because each heir has authority over his own right; he can waive his right to object. The hadith explicitly allows this: 'except if the heirs wish.' The principle is that the heirs' refusal to consent is a right they can exercise or relinquish.

Key Terms
اجازت (ijazah): Permission or ratification given by the heirs after the testator's death to validate a bequest that would otherwise be invalid.
رد (radd): Rejection or refusal of a bequest by an heir, resulting in the bequest being invalid with respect to that heir's share.
ولایت (wilayah): Authority or control a person has over his own rights; here, each heir has wilayah over his own share, so he can consent or reject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man makes a bequest to his nephew, who is an heir. After the man dies, two of his three heirs consent, and the third rejects. What is the ruling?
A) The entire bequest is invalid because one heir objected.
B) The bequest is valid only from the shares of the two consenting heirs, and void from the rejecting heir's share.
C) The bequest is valid if the consenting heirs have a majority.
D) The bequest is invalid unless all heirs consent.

Key Takeaway
When some heirs consent to a bequest for an heir, the bequest is valid from their shares and void from the shares of those who reject.

Bequest Between Muslim and Non-Muslim: Dhimmi vs. Harbi
Ruling with proof on bequest to non-Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequests to dhimmis and harbis, cite the Quranic evidence, and identify the exception for musta'min.

Core Idea
A bequest to a dhimmi is valid as a form of kindness; a bequest to a harbi is invalid as forbidden alliance.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between two categories of non-Muslims when it comes to bequests: dhimmis under Muslim protection and harbis in a state of war. Using Quran 60:8-9, the madhhab permits bequests to dhimmis and prohibits them to harbis, unless the harbi has obtained safe conduct (aman). This lesson unpacks the reasoning and evidence behind these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on bequests (wasiyyah) between Muslims and non-Muslims. Determine the hukm for each category.
The act is tabarru' (donation) via bequest.
2
Distinguish dhimmi vs. harbi
Separate non-Muslims into two groups based on their contractual relationship with the Islamic state: dhimmis (protected citizens) and harbis (enemy combatants).
The source also mentions musta'min (safe-conduct holder) as an exception.
3
Locate the dalil
Two Quranic verses are cited: Quran 60:8 for permissibility with dhimmis, and Quran 60:9 for prohibition with harbis.
Both verses are from Surah al-Mumtahanah.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each verse proves the ruling. Verse 8 allows kindness (birr) to non-fighters, implying bequest is a form of kindness. Verse 9 forbids alliance (tawalli) with fighters, so bequest as a form of alliance is invalid.
The Hanafi usul principle equates bequest with alliance in this context.
5
Note the exception and cross-madhhab difference
A harbi who becomes musta'min is treated like a dhimmi. Compare with Shafi'i view that allows bequest to any non-Muslim.
This highlights the importance of contractual status in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز ان يوصى المسلم للكافر والكافر للمسلم فالاول لقوله تعالى لا ينهاكم الله عن الذين لم يقاتلوكم في الدين الاية والثاني لانهم بعقد الذمة ساووا المسلمين فى المعاملات ولهذا جاز التبرع من الجانبين في حالة الحيوة فكذا بعد الممات وفى الجامع الصغير الوصية لاهل الحزب باطلة لقوله تعالى انما ينها كم الله عن الذين قاتلوكم في الدين الاية
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جائز ہے کہ مسلمان کافر کے لئے اور کا فرمسلمان کے لئے وصیت کرے پس اول اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان لا ينها كمُ الله الخ کی وجہ سے اور ثانی اس لئے کہ کفار عقد ذمہ کی وجہ سے معاملات کے اندر مسلمانوں کے برابر ہو گئے اس لئے حالت حیات میں جانین سے تبرع جائز ہے پس ایسے ہی مرنے کے بعد اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ اہل حرب کے لئے وصیت باطل ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے فرمان انما ينها كم الله الخ کی وجہ ہے۔
تشریح مسلمان ذمی کے لئے اور ذقی مسلمان کے لئے وصیت کرے تو جائز ہے کیونکہ وصیت ایک تبرع ہے اور اہل ذمہ بھی تبرع واحسان کے اہل ہیں البتہ وہ کا فرحر بی جو دار الحرب میں ہے اس کے لئے وصیت باطل ہے ہاں اگر وہ مستامن ہو تو اس کا حکم بھی ذقی کے مل ہے، لہذا مصنف نے جواز کے لئے پہلی آیت اور بطلان کے لئے دوسری آیت پیش کی ہے۔
پہلی آیت لابنها كم الله عن الذين لم يُقَاتِلو اكم فى الدين ولم يُخرجُو كمْ مِنْ دِيَار كم أن تَبرُّ وَ هُمْ وَ تقطوا اليهم، اللہ تعالیٰ تم کو ان لوگوں کے ساتھ بھلائی اور انصاف کا سلوک کرنے سے منع نہیں کرتا جو نہ دین کے بارے میں تم سے لڑتے ہیں اور نہ انہوں نے تم کو تمہارے گھروں سے نکالا ہے۔ تو اس آپ سے ذمیوں کے لئے زندگی میں تبرع واحسان کا جواز ثابت ہوا اور ساتھ ہی ساتھ یہ بھی ثابت ہو گیا کہ ان کے لئے وصیت بھی جائز ہے۔
دوسری آیت إِنما يَنْهَاكُمُ اللهُ عَنِ الَّذِينَ قَاتَلَُوْ كُمْ فِى الدِّينِ وَاَخَرَ جُوَاكُمْ مِنْ دِيَا رِكُمْ وَظَاهَرُ وَ اعَلَىٰ إِخْرَاجكم ان تَوَلَّوهُمُ " اللہ تعالیٰ تم کو ان لوگوں کے ساتھ دوستی کرنے سے منع کرتا ہے جو تم سے دین کے بارے میں لڑے اور تم کو تمہارے گھروں سے نکالا اور تمہارے نکالنے میں شریک ہوئے ، اس آیت سے جیسے یہ معلوم ہوا کہ تربیوں سے دوستی کرنا ممنوع ہے اسی طرح یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ ان کے لئے وصیت کرنا باطل ہے تو اس کے لئے وصیت کیسے جائز ہوسکتی ہے۔
He said: It is permissible for a Muslim to make a bequest to a disbeliever and for a disbeliever to a Muslim. The first is due to the saying of Allah: 'Allah does not forbid you from those who did not fight you in religion...' And the second because by the dhimma contract they equaled Muslims in transactions. Thus, donations are permissible from both sides during life, so also after death. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir, a bequest to the people of war is invalid due to the saying of Allah: 'Allah only forbids you from those who fought you in religion...' Translation: Al-Quduri said: It is permissible for a Muslim to make a bequest to a disbeliever and for a disbeliever to a Muslim. The first is due to Allah's command 'Allah does not forbid you...' and the second because disbelievers, by the dhimma contract, became equal to Muslims in transactions, so donations are permissible from both sides during life, so also after death. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir, a bequest to the people of war is invalid because of Allah's saying: 'Allah only forbids you...' Explanation: A Muslim making a bequest to a dhimmi and a dhimmi to a Muslim is permissible because a bequest is a donation, and dhimmis are worthy of donations and kindness. However, for a harbi (one at war) who is in dar al-harb, a bequest is invalid unless he is a musta'min (those granted safe conduct), in which case his ruling is like that of a dhimmi. Therefore, the author presented the first verse for permissibility and the second for invalidity. First verse: 'Allah does not forbid you from those who did not fight you in religion and did not expel you from your homes, that you be righteous and just toward them.' From this, the permissibility of donation and kindness to dhimmis during life is established, and also that a bequest to them is permissible. Second verse: 'Allah only forbids you from those who fought you in religion and expelled you from your homes and aided in your expulsion, that you take them as allies.' From this, it is understood that taking them as allies is forbidden, and likewise making a bequest to them is invalid; so how can a bequest to them be permissible?
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of bequests between Muslims and non-Muslims under certain conditions. It distinguishes between two categories: dhimmis (non-Muslim citizens of the Islamic state) and harbis (enemy combatants not under Muslim protection). For dhimmis, bequests in both directions are permissible because dhimmis have a covenant of protection and are treated equally in financial transactions. This is supported by Quran 60:8 which allows kindness to those who do not fight Muslims. For harbis, bequests are invalid because they are at war with Muslims; Quran 60:9 forbids friendship with them, and bequest is a form of friendship. However, if a harbi enters Muslim territory with safe conduct (musta'min), he is treated like a dhimmi, and bequests to or from him become valid. The author cites al-Jami' al-Saghir for the invalidity of bequests to 'ahl al-harb' (people of war). The ruling is based on the principle that wasiyyah is a form of charitable donation (tabarru'), and those eligible to receive charity in life are also eligible to receive bequests.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under the protection of the Islamic state, paying jizyah, and enjoying rights including property and transaction rights.
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is not under Muslim protection and is in a state of war or enmity with the Islamic state.
مستأمن (musta'min): A harbi who enters Muslim lands with safe conduct (aman) for a temporary period.
تبرع (tabarru'): A voluntary donation or charitable act, including gifts and bequests.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A Muslim man makes a bequest to a non-Muslim who lives in a non-Muslim country and is at war with Muslims. What is the ruling?
A) The bequest is valid if the non-Muslim is a dhimmi.
B) The bequest is invalid if the non-Muslim is a harbi.
C) The bequest is always invalid.
D) The bequest is valid regardless of status.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of a bequest to a non-Muslim depends on their contractual status: valid for dhimmis and musta'min, invalid for harbis.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
Acceptance of Bequest Only Valid After Testator's Death
Ruling that acceptance/rejection of bequest before death is invalid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that acceptance of a bequest must occur after the testator's death, and distinguish this from hibah and inheritance.

Core Idea
Accepting a bequest before death is void — the ruling attaches only after death.

In the Hanafi school, a bequest (wasiyyah) is a deferred transfer of ownership that takes effect only after the testator's death. This lesson examines a key condition: the legatee's acceptance (qabūl) must occur after death. Al-Quduri's matn, explained by the commentator, makes clear that any acceptance or rejection during the testator's lifetime is legally void. We'll explore the reasoning and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is the legatee's acceptance or rejection of a bequest while the testator is alive. The ruling is that it is invalid (bāṭil).
The ruling applies to both acceptance and rejection equally.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The proof is qiyās (analogical reasoning): the bequest's ruling (hukm) is attached to death, so acceptance before death is like acceptance before a contract—premature and ineffective.
The text says 'as it is not considered before a contract'.
3
Distinguish Bequest from Inheritance and Hibah
Inheritance does not require acceptance because it is by way of substitution (khilāfah). Hibah requires acceptance but takes effect immediately. Bequest shares the 'new ownership' nature of hibah but is deferred to after death.
This distinction clarifies why the timing condition is unique.
4
Note the Istihsān Exception
If both testator and legatee die without the legatee having accepted, the bequeathed property passes to the legatee's heirs by istihsān (juristic preference). This is an exception to the rule requiring acceptance.
This exception shows flexibility within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وقبول الوصية بعد الموت فان قبلها الموصى له في حال حياته او ردها فذلك باطل لان أوان ثبوت حكمه بعد الموت لتعلقه به فلا يعتبر قبله كما لا يعتبر قبل العقد
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور وصیت کا قبول کرنا موت کے بعد ہے پس اگر موصی لہ نے موصی کی زندگی میں وصیت کو قبول کیا تو یہ باطل ہے اس لئے کہ وصیت کا حکم ثابت ہونے کا وقت موت کے بعد ہے وصیت کے متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے موت کے ساتھ تو قبول ورد موت سے پہلے معتبر نہ ہو گا جیسے عقد سے پہلے معتبر نہیں ہوتا ۔
تشریح میراث کے اندر یہ شرط نہیں کہ وارث قبول بھی کرے کیونکہ میراث میں اسباب ہی نہیں کہ اس کو قبول کرنے کی حاجت پیش آئے گی بلکہ ارث تو بطریق خلافت ہے اور ہبہ میں جیسے ملک جدید حاصل ہوتی ہے اسی طرح وصیت کے اندر بھی ملک جدید حاصل ہوتی ہے تو وصیت کے اندر جو از وصیت کے لئے اگر چہ موصی لہ کا قبول کرنا شرط نہیں ہے لیکن موضی بہ کا مالک ہو جانے کے لئے قبول موصی لا شرط ہے البتہ بعض صورتیں ایسی ہیں کہ جو بلا قبول موضی لہ استحسانا جائز ہیں جیسے بعد وصیت موصی کا انتقال ہو جائے پھر بلا قبول ور د کے موضی لیہ کا بھی انتقال ہو جائے تو استحسانا موضی یہ موصی لیڈ کے ورثہ کا ہوگا۔
بہر حال اس تفصیل سے معلوم ہوا کہ موضعی لا کے مملوک ہونے کے لئے موصی لہا کی جانب سے قبول ہونا چاہئے۔ مگر یہ قبول موضعی کی موت کے بعد ہونا چاہئے موسی کی زندگی میں جو قبول و رد موضعی لانے کیا ہے اس کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے کیونکہ جیسے اس قبول کا اعتبار نہیں ہے جو عقد وصیت سے پہلے ہو ایسے ہی اس قبول کا اعتبار نہیں ہے جو موصی کی حیات میں ہو جس کی وجہ واضح ہے کہ حکم وصیت کا ثبوت بعد موت ہوتا ہے لہذا قبول بھی اسی وقت معتبر ہو گا۔
He said: Acceptance of a bequest is after death. If the legatee accepts or rejects it during his lifetime, that is invalid, because the time for establishing its ruling is after death due to its attachment to it, so it is not considered before that, just as it is not considered before the contract. Commentary: Al-Quduri stated that acceptance of a bequest is after death. If the legatee accepts the bequest during the testator's lifetime, it is invalid because the time for the bequest's ruling to be established is after death due to its attachment to death, so acceptance and rejection before death are not valid, just as they are not valid before a contract. Elaboration: In inheritance, it is not a condition that the heir accepts, because inheritance does not require acceptance; it is by way of substitution (khilafah). In hibah (gift), ownership is acquired anew, similarly in bequest ownership is acquired anew. So for the bequest, acceptance by the legatee is a condition for becoming owner of the bequeathed item, though some cases are permitted without acceptance by istihsan, e.g., if the testator dies then the legatee also dies without acceptance, the bequeathed item becomes the property of the legatee's heirs by istihsan. In any case, for the legatee to become owner, acceptance is required, but this acceptance must occur after the testator's death. Acceptance or rejection during the testator's lifetime is not considered, just as acceptance before a bequest contract is not considered, because the ruling of the bequest is established after death, so acceptance is only valid at that time.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Al-Quduri's matn, commented upon by the author of Ashraf al-Hidayah. It states a fundamental principle: a bequest (wasiyyah) is a transfer of ownership that takes effect after the testator's death. Therefore, any acceptance or rejection by the legatee during the testator's lifetime is legally void. The reasoning is that the ruling (hukm) of the bequest is attached to death, so its time of effectiveness is after death. Just as acceptance before a contract is invalid, acceptance before the testator's death is also invalid. The commentator distinguishes bequest from inheritance, where no acceptance is needed because the heir inherits by way of substitution (khilafah), and from hibah (gift), which is effective immediately. The bequest is like hibah in that ownership is acquired anew, but unlike hibah, the transfer is deferred to after death. The commentator also notes exceptions by istihsan: if the testator and legatee both die without the legatee having accepted, the bequeathed property passes to the legatee's heirs. The key takeaway is that the legatee's acceptance must be after the testator's death; prior acceptance is of no consequence.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): A disposition of property that takes effect after the testator's death, transferring ownership to the legatee.
موصى له (mūṣā lahu): The legatee, the person who receives the bequest.
قبول (qabūl): Acceptance; the action by which the legatee agrees to receive the bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the legatee might change his mind after death
B) Because the ruling of the bequest is established only after death, so acceptance before that is premature
C) Because the testator might revoke the bequest
D) Because acceptance must be in the presence of witnesses

Key Takeaway
Acceptance of a bequest must occur after the testator's death; any prior acceptance or rejection is void.

Recommendation to Bequeath Less Than One-Third and Preference Based on Heirs' Wealth
Ruling on recommended bequest amount and preference based on heirs' need

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recommended amount of bequest and explain the preference between bequeathing and leaving the bequest based on the heirs' financial condition.

Core Idea
Bequeathing less than one-third is recommended; the choice between bequeathing and leaving it depends on whether heirs are poor or rich.

In this passage, Al-Quduri establishes the general recommendation to bequeath less than one-third of one's estate, regardless of the heirs' wealth. The commentator then expands on a secondary question: when is it better to actually make a bequest versus leaving no bequest at all? The answer hinges on the financial condition of the heirs, leading to an intra-Hanafi discussion on which virtuous act – charity to a non-relative or maintaining ties with a relative – takes precedence. Understanding this conditional preference helps you apply the rulings of wasiyyah with proper consideration of the heirs' needs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and its basis
The passage states it is mustahabb to bequeath less than one-third, whether heirs are rich or poor. The reason is that reducing the bequest leaves more for heirs, which is an act of maintaining family ties (silat al-rahm).
One-third is the maximum allowed for bequests to non-heirs; less is recommended.
2
Recognize the secondary question
After the general ruling, the author asks: Is it better to actually make a bequest (less than one-third) or to leave no bequest at all? This is not about validity but about which action carries greater reward.
This is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Apply the condition: poor heirs
If the heirs are poor and the inheritance will not make them self-sufficient, leaving the bequest (i.e., not bequeathing) is better. This is because the wealth then becomes sadaqah (charity) to a relative, which is the best charity as per the hadith.
Hadith: 'Afḍal al-ṣadaqah ʿalā dhī al-raḥim al-kāshiḥ' (Musnad Ahmad).
4
Apply the condition: rich heirs
If the heirs are rich or will become rich through their share, then bequeathing to a non-relative is better, because it is pure charity seeking Allah's pleasure. However, some scholars give the testator a choice (takhyeer) between bequeathing and leaving it, since both are virtuous.
The text presents the first view as primary; the second is a minority intra-Hanafi opinion.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The dispute is about virtue (afḍaliyyah), not validity. Both bequeathing and leaving no bequest are valid; the difference is in the reward and which action is considered better in each scenario.
This does not affect the legal validity of the will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويستحب ان يوصى الانسان بدون الثلث سواء كانت الورثة اغنياء او فقراء لان في التنقيص صلة القريب بترك ماله عليهم بخلاف استكمال الثلث لانه استيفاء تمام حقه فلا صلة ولا منة ثم الوصيه باقل من الثلث اولى ام تركها قالوا ان كانت الورثة فقراء ولا يستغنون بمايرثون فالترك اولى لما فيه من الصدقة على القريب وقد قال عليه السلام افضل الصدقة على ذى الرحم الكاشح ولان فيه رعاية حق الفقراء والقرابة جميعا
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور مستحب ہے یہ کہ انسان ثلث سے کم کی وصیت کرے خواہ ورثہ مالدار ہوں یا فقراء اس لئے کہ ثلث سے کم کرنے میں قریبی رشتہ دار پر صلہ رحمی کرنا ہے ان پر اپنے مال کو چھوڑنے کے ساتھ بخلاف ثلث کو مکمل کر لینے کے اس لئے کہ یہ تو اپنا حق پورا وصول کر لینا ہے تو یہ نہ صلہ ہے اور نہ کوئی احسان ہے پھر تہائی سے کم وصیت کرنا اولی ہے یا وصیت کا ترک (اولی) ہے مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ اگر ورثہ تنگدست ہوں اور مقدار میراث سے وہ تو نگر نہ ہوں تو وصیت کا ترک اولی ہے کیونکہ اس میں قریب پر صلہ ہے اور نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ بہترین صدقہ ایسے ذی رحم پر ہے جس سے وہ خوش نہ ہو اور اس لئے کہ اس میں فقراء اور قرابت دونوں کی رعایت ہے۔
تشریح شریعت نے انسان کو اس کے آخری لمحات میں اپنے تہائی مال میں تصرف کا اختیار دیا ہے لہذا تہائی میں اس کے لئے وصیت کرنا جائز ہے لیکن اس کے لئے مستحب یہ ہے کہ ورثہ خواہ مالدار ہوں یا غریب پوری تہائی کی وصیت نہ کرے بلکہ کم کی وصیت کرے اس لئے کہ کم کی وصیت کرنے کی صورت میں جو اس نے اپنا مال اپنے ورثہ کے لئے چھوڑا ہے تو اس میں اپنے اعزہ واقر بہ کے ساتھ حسن سلوک اور صلہ ہے جو محمود فعل ہے اور اگر اس نے پورے تہائی کی وصیت کر دی تو اس نے اپنا حق وصول کرلیا تو یہ کوئی صلہ اور احسان اور حسن سلوک نہیں ہے، بہر حال ثلث سے کم کی وصیت کرے۔ پھر یہاں یہ سوال پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ ثلث سے کم کی وصیت کرنا اولیٰ ہے یا اس کو چھوڑ دینا اولی ہے تو فقہاء نے اس کی کچھ تفصیل کی ہے چنانچہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر ورثہ غریب ہوں اور میراث کی جو مقدار انھیں ملے گی اس سے وہ تو نگر اور غنی نہیں ہو نگے تو ایسی صورت میں وصیت نہ کرنا افضل واولی ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں قریب پر صلہ کا ثواب ملے گا اور اس صورت میں فقراء اور قرابت دونوں حقوں کی رعایت ہے۔
اور مسند احمد میں روایت ہے" افضل الصدقة على ذى الرحم الكاشح یعنی اپنے ذی رقم پر صدقہ کرنا افضل ہے جس سے آدمی خوش نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس میں نفس کی مخالفت ہے۔
ورثہ مالدار ہوں تو وصیت کرنا افضل ہے یا ترک وصیت؟
وان كانو اغنياء اويستغنون بنصيبهم فالوصية اولى لانه يكون صدقة على الاجنبى والترك هبة من القريب والاولى اولى لانه يبتغي بها وجه الله تعالى وقيل في هذا الوجه يخير لاشتمال كل منهما على فضيلة وهو الصدقة او الصلة فيخيرين بين الخيرين.
ترجمہ اور اگر ورثہ مالدار ہوں یا وہ اپنے حصہ سے مالدار ہو جائیں گے تو وصیت اولی ہے اس لئے کہ وصیت اجنبی پر صدقہ ہوگا اور ترک وصیت قریب پر ہبہ ہوگا اور اول (صدقہ ) اولی اور افضل ہے ( ہبہ سے ) اس لئے کہ صدقہ سے اللہ تعالیٰ کی رضا مندی کو تلاش کیا جاتا ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ اس صورت میں موصی کو اختیار ہے ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے ایک فضیلت پر مشتمل ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ صدقہ یا صلہ ہے تو موصی کو دونوں نیکیوں کے درمیان اختیار دیا جائے گا۔
He said: It is recommended that a person bequeath less than one-third, whether the heirs are rich or poor, because in reducing (the bequest) there is maintaining family ties by leaving one's wealth for them, unlike completing the one-third, because that is taking one's full right, so there is no tie or favor. Then, is bequeathing less than one-third better or leaving it? They said: If the heirs are poor and will not be independent with what they inherit, then leaving it is better, because in it is charity to a relative, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The best charity is to a relative who is hostile,' and because it observes the rights of the poor and kinship together. Translation: Al-Quduri said: It is recommended that a person bequeath less than one-third, whether the heirs are rich or poor, because in reducing there is maintaining family ties by leaving one's wealth for them, unlike completing the one-third, because that is taking one's full right, so it is neither a tie nor a favor. Then, is bequeathing less than one-third better or leaving it? The scholars said: If the heirs are poor and will not be independent with what they inherit, then leaving it is better, because in it is charity to a relative, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The best charity is to a relative who is hostile,' and because it observes the rights of the poor and kinship together. Commentary: The Shariah has given a person permission to dispose of up to one-third of his wealth in his final moments, so bequeathing one-third is permissible, but it is recommended that he not bequeath the full one-third but less, regardless of whether the heirs are rich or poor. This is because by bequeathing less, he leaves more wealth for his heirs, which is kindness and maintaining ties (silat rahm), a praiseworthy act. If he bequeaths the full one-third, he merely takes his own right, which involves no kindness or favor. So he should bequeath less than one-third. Then the question arises: is bequeathing less than one-third better, or leaving the bequest (i.e., not bequeathing at all) better? The jurists have detailed this: if the heirs are poor and the inheritance they receive will not make them self-sufficient, then not bequeathing is better and more virtuous, because by leaving the wealth to them, he gets the reward of maintaining ties, and this considers both the rights of the poor and kinship. There is a narration in Musnad Ahmad: 'The best charity is to a relative who is hostile,' meaning the relative with whom one is not pleased, because it involves opposing one's nafs. If the heirs are rich or will become rich through their share, then bequeathing is better, because the bequest becomes charity to a non-relative, whereas leaving it is a gift to a relative. The first (charity) is better because it seeks the pleasure of Allah. And it is said that in this case the testator has a choice, since each option contains a virtue: charity or maintaining ties, so he chooses between the two good deeds.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended amount of bequest and the preference between making a bequest and leaving the wealth to heirs. It begins by stating that it is mustahabb (recommended) to bequeath less than one-third, whether the heirs are rich or poor. The reason is that by bequeathing less, the testator leaves more for his relatives, which is an act of maintaining family ties (silat rahm). If he bequeaths the full one-third, he simply exercises his legal right but does no favor. Then the commentator addresses whether bequeathing less than one-third is better than leaving no bequest at all. The scholars differentiate based on the heirs' financial condition: if the heirs are poor and the inheritance will not make them self-sufficient, then not bequeathing is better, because leaving wealth to poor relatives counts as charity (sadaqah) to a relative, which is the best form of charity as per the hadith: 'The best charity is to a relative who is hostile.' This covers both the right of the poor and the right of kinship. If the heirs are rich or will become rich through their share, then bequeathing to a non-relative is better, because it is pure charity seeking Allah's pleasure, whereas leaving it to rich relatives is merely a gift. However, some scholars say the testator has a choice in this scenario, as both acts have their own virtue: charity to a non-relative versus maintaining ties with a relative. The testator may choose whichever he prefers.

Key Terms
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the estate, the maximum proportion that can be bequeathed to non-heirs in Hanafi law.
مستحب (mustahab): Recommended; an action that is rewarded but not obligatory.
صلة الرحم (ṣilat al-raḥim): Maintaining family ties, considered a virtuous act in Islam.
صدقة (ṣadaqah): Charity given voluntarily to seek Allah's reward.
كاشح (kāshiḥ): A relative who harbors enmity or displeasure; giving to such a person is especially meritorious because it involves opposing one's nafs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is it better for a testator to leave no bequest (i.e., not bequeath any part of the one-third)?
A) When the heirs are rich and do not need the inheritance
B) When the heirs are poor and will not be self-sufficient with the inheritance
C) When the testator has no relatives
D) When the testator wants to give charity to a non-relative

Key Takeaway
Bequeathing less than one-third is recommended; the choice between bequeathing and leaving it depends on whether heirs are poor (leave it) or rich (bequeath to a non-relative).

Preference of Bequest vs No Bequest Based on Heirs' Wealth
Determining preference between bequest and no bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the preference between a bequest of less than one-third and no bequest, and apply the condition regarding heirs' wealth to determine which is more virtuous.

Core Idea
Leaving a bequest of less than one-third is recommended, but if heirs are poor, leaving no bequest is more virtuous because it maintains family ties.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a practical question for a dying person: should he make a small bequest to non-relatives, or leave his entire wealth to his heirs? The answer depends on the financial state of the heirs. The Shariah allows bequeathing up to one-third, but the virtuous choice varies. We will explore the Hanafi position and the evidence from hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the general recommendation: it is mustahabb to bequeath less than one-third, whether heirs are rich or poor.
The passage says 'mustahabb' in the commentary.
2
Recognize the condition
Understand how the financial status of heirs affects the preference: if heirs are needy, leaving no bequest is better; if they are wealthy, making a bequest is better.
This is based on the mashaa'ikh's detail.
3
Understand the evidence
Examine the hadith cited: 'The best charity is upon a resentful relative.' It supports the virtue of leaving wealth to needy relatives.
Hadith from Musnad Ahmad.
4
Note the intra-school variation
When heirs are wealthy, there are two views: bequest is better (preferred) or the testator has a choice.
The second view is introduced with 'qil' (it is said).
5
Apply the ruling
Given a testator scenario with known heir wealth, determine whether bequest or no bequest is more virtuous.
Use the mufta bihi view.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹ سے کم کرنے میں قریبی رشتہ دار پر صلہ رحمی کرنا ہے ان پر اپنے مال کو چھوڑنے کے ساتھ بخلاف ثلث کو مکمل کر لینے کے اس لئے کہ یہ تو اپنا حق پورا وصول کر لینا ہے تو یہ نہ صلہ ہے اور نہ کوئی احسان ہے پھر تہائی سے کم وصیت کرنا اولی ہے یا وصیت کا ترک (اولی) ہے مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ اگر ورثہ تنگدست ہوں اور مقدار میراث سے وہ تو نگر نہ ہوں تو وصیت کا ترک اولی ہے کیونکہ اس میں قریب پر صلہ ہے اور نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ بہترین صدقہ ایسے ذی رحم پر ہے جس سے وہ خوش نہ ہو اور اس لئے کہ اس میں فقراء اور قرابت دونوں کی رعایت ہے۔
